Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
12 min
Mistaken Killing in Battle and Shared Causation in Diyah
Two rulings: mistaken killing in battle and shared causation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Muslim who mistakenly kills another Muslim in battle (no qisas, but diyah and kaffarah), and calculate diyah liability when death results from multiple independent causes including a human act, self-harm, and animal attacks (one-third on the human).

Core Idea
Mistaken killing in battle requires diyah and kaffarah, not qisas; shared causation reduces liability to one-third.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents two important rulings from the Hanafi school on diyat (blood money). First, when a Muslim kills another Muslim on the battlefield believing him to be a disbeliever, the killer is not subject to qisas but must pay kaffarah and diyah. Second, when death occurs due to a combination of causes—the victim's own act, another person's act, and animal attacks—only the human act carries liability, and the diyah is divided proportionally. We will examine the legal reasoning and the Quranic proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
The base text states no qisas for a Muslim killing a Muslim mistaken as a disbeliever in battle. Instead, kaffarah and diyah are due. Note the context: meeting of two battle lines.
The killer's intention is to kill a disbeliever, but the victim is a Muslim.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
The commentary cites Surah al-Nisa' 4:92, which prescribes kaffarah and diyah for accidental killing. The term 'khata'an' (mistake) includes this scenario.
The verse is explicit about the penalty for mistaken killing.
3
Note the exception
If the victim was in the polytheists' row, his immunity (ismah) is lost because he swelled their numbers, so no diyah is due. This is based on a hadith: 'Whoever increases the numbers of a people, he is from them.'
The exception applies when the Muslim victim is physically aligned with the enemy.
4
Analyze the second scenario: causation analysis
Death caused by three factors: victim's self-action, Zaid's action, and actions of a wild beast and a snake. The beast and snake are considered 'hadr' (legally void), as is the victim's own act. Only Zaid's act remains, so he pays one-third of the diyah.
The key principle: acts that are legally wasted (hadr) do not create liability.
5
Summarize the principle
When death is attributed to multiple independent agents, each agent's liability is assessed separately. Acts that are inherently devoid of legal consequence (hadr) are excluded, and only human acts with culpability remain. The diyah is divided proportionally among the responsible parties.
The same principle applies in modern tort law for apportioning damages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا في قتل مسلم مسلماً ظنه مشركاً عند التقاء الصفين، بل يكفرُ ويَدِي : أي يعطي الدِّية. وفي موت بفعل نفسه وزيد وسبع وحيّةٍ ثلث الدِّيةِ على زيد؛ لأَنَّهُ ماتَ بثلاثة أفعال، ففعلُ السبع والحيّة جنس واحد لكونه هدرا مطلقاً، وفعل نفسه هدر، وبقي فعل زيد وحده، فيجب عليه ثلث الدية. قوله : ولا في قتل مسلم مسلماً ظنه مشركا ... الخ؛ يعني إذا التقى صفان من المشركين والمسلمين، فقتل مسلم مسلماً بظن أنه مشرك، فلا قصاص عليه بل الكفارة؛ لأنَّ هذا أحد نوعي الخطأ، والخطأ بنوعيه لا يوجبُ القَوَد، بل يوجب الكفارة، وكذا الدية على ما نطق به الكتاب وهو قوله : وَمَن قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَنًا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ وَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَّمَةٌ الآية. ولما اختلف سيوف المسلمين على إيمان أبي حذيفة قضى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالدية، هذا إذا كانا مختلطين، أما إذا كان المسلم في صف المشركين فلا تجب الدية لسقوط عصمته بتكثيرِ سوادهم؛ لقوله : (من كثر سواد قوم فهو منهم)، أخرجه أبو يعلى الموصلي في مسنده عن عمر بن الحارث عن ابن مسعود .
And not (qisas) for a Muslim killing a Muslim whom he thought to be a disbeliever at the meeting of the two rows (battle lines); rather he must expiate (kaffarah) and pay blood money: i.e. gives diyah. And regarding death caused by the act of himself, Zaid, a wild beast, and a snake: one-third of the diyah is upon Zaid; because he died by three acts: the act of the wild beast and the snake are of one type because they are absolutely wasted (hadr), and his own act is wasted, and only Zaid's act remains, so one-third diyah is obligatory upon him. His statement: 'And not for a Muslim killing a Muslim whom he thought to be a disbeliever...' meaning when two rows of polytheists and Muslims meet, and a Muslim kills a Muslim thinking him a polytheist, there is no retaliation upon him but rather kaffarah; because this is one type of mistake, and mistake in both its types does not necessitate retaliation, but rather necessitates kaffarah, and likewise diyah as the Book states: 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then freeing a believing slave and a diyah paid to his family' verse. And when the swords of the Muslims differed concerning the faith of Abu Hudhayfah, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ruled for diyah. This is when they are intermingled; but if the Muslim is in the polytheist's row, then diyah is not obligatory because his inviolability is lost by increasing their numbers; according to his saying: 'Whoever increases the numbers of a people, he is from them'—narrated by Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili in his Musnad from 'Umar ibn al-Harith from Ibn Mas'ud.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings. First, if a Muslim kills another Muslim in battle mistakenly believing him to be a disbeliever, no qisas is imposed; instead, kaffarah (expiation) and diyah (blood money) are obligatory. The Quranic basis is verse 4:92. The commentary clarifies that if the deceased Muslim was fighting alongside the polytheists (in their row), his immunity is lost because he swelled their numbers, so no diyah is due, based on a hadith. Second, the case of death caused by multiple agents: a person (Zaid), the victim himself, a wild beast, and a snake. The death is attributed to three independent acts: the victim's own act (self-inflicted), the wild beast and snake (both classified as hadr—no liability), and Zaid's act. Since only Zaid's act carries potential liability, he pays one-third of the diyah. The explanation assumes that the wild beast and snake are analogous and their acts are legally void.

Key Terms
قتل خطأ (qatl khata'): Mistaken killing, including where the killer intends to hit a disbeliever but kills a Muslim.
هدر (hadr): Legally wasted; no liability for blood money or penalty.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the family of the victim in cases where qisas is not applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a Muslim killed by a Muslim in battle due to mistaken identity, what is the penalty?
A) Qisas is obligatory.
B) Diyah and kaffarah are required.
C) No penalty because of war circumstances.
D) Only kaffarah, no diyah.

Key Takeaway
Mistaken killing in battle does not warrant qisas but requires diyah and kaffarah; when multiple causes contribute to death, liability is assessed per cause, and only human acts carry diyah.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diya for Killing an Insane or Minor Attacker
Ruling on diya for killing an insane person or boy, with intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diya for killing an insane or minor attacker, explain the basis for differences with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, and apply the ruling to a new scenario.

Core Idea
Killing an insane attacker requires diya, not qisas, because the attacker lacks full legal capacity.

This lesson examines the legal consequences when a sane person kills an insane person or a minor who draws a sword and attacks. The relied-upon Hanafi view holds that diya (blood money) is obligatory because the attacker's immunity (ismah) is not fully extinguished, even though qisas is not applicable due to lack of legal capacity. The passage presents two opposing views: within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf denies any liability, while al-Shafi'i argues for complete immunity based on self-defense. Understanding the reasoning behind each position strengthens your ability to apply Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act and the ruling: killing an insane person or boy who draws a sword on you. According to the mufta bihi view, diya is wajib. Note that qisas is not applicable because the attacker is not mukallaf.
The text opens with 'ويجب الدية' – diya is obligatory.
2
Identify the opposing views
Two opposing positions are presented: (1) Abu Yusuf (intra-Hanafi) holds no diya, likening the act to an animal injury. (2) Al-Shafi'i holds no liability at all, analogizing to a sane adult in self-defense.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on the legal insignificance of the act; al-Shafi'i's on self-defense.
3
Examine the opposing proofs
For Abu Yusuf: the acts of a boy/insane person are not legally considered for liability – just as an animal's injury is 'jubar' (free). For al-Shafi'i: the killing is self-defense, and the attacker's immunity is temporarily lost, as with a sane adult.
Al-Shafi'i's analogy relies on the idea that the defender is compelled to kill.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: a sane adult's immunity is fully lost during an attack, but an insane or minor attacker never had full immunity in the first place. Therefore, diya is due because the defender took a life that was still protected (though imperfectly).
The text also refutes Abu Yusuf's animal analogy by distinguishing owned animals from the attacker's own immunity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under the mufta bihi, the defender pays diya. Under Abu Yusuf, no payment. Under al-Shafi'i, no payment. Also, the mufta bihi view imposes liability on the owner if the attacker is an animal.
This shows how a difference in legal reasoning leads to different financial outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجبُ الدِّيةُ بقتل مجنون أو صبي شهر سيفاً على رجل فقتله هو [٢] قوله : ويجب الدية... الخ ; أي وإن شهر المجنون أو الصبي سيفاً على رجل فقتله المشهورُ عليه عمداً يجب الدية ، قال في تكملة البحر (۲): وعلى هذا الدابة، وعن أبي يوسف : لا تجب الدية في الصبي المجنون. وقال الشافعي له : لا يجب الضمان في الكلّ ; لأنه قتله دافعاً عن النفس، فصار كالبالغ العاقل، وهذا لأنه يصيرُ محمولاً على قتله بفعله، كأن قال له : اقتلني وإلا قتلتك، وكون الدابة مملوكة للغير لا تأثير له في وجوب الضمان، كالعبد إذا شَهْرَ سيفاً على رجل فقتله، فإنّه لا يجب الضمان، فكذا هذا ، فصار كالعبد إذا صال على الحرّ فقتله. ولأبي يوسف : إن فعل الصبي والمجنون معتبر أصلاً حتى لا يعتبر في حق وجوب الضمان ; لأنّ جناية العجماء جبار، وكذا عصمتها لحقها، وعصمةُ الدَّابة لحق المالك، فكان فعلهما مسقطاً لحقهما بعصمتِهما فلا يضمنان ، ويضمنُ الدابةُ بخلاف الصيد إذا صال على المحرم أو صيد الحرم على الحلال ; لأنّ الشارع أذن في قتله، ولم يوجب علينا بحمل أذاه. ألا ترى أن الخمس الفواسق أباح قتلها مطلقاً ; لتوهم الأذى منها، فما ظنك في إذا تحقق الأذى ومالك الدابة لم يأذن ، فيجب الضمان، وكذا عصمة عبد الغير لحق نفسه، وفعله محظور، فسقط به عصمته.
And diya is obligatory for killing an insane person or a boy who draws a sword upon a man and kills him. [2] His saying: 'And diya is obligatory... etc.' That is, if an insane person or a boy draws a sword upon a man and the one upon whom it is drawn kills him intentionally, diya is obligatory. He said in Takmilah al-Bahr (2): And likewise for an animal. From Abu Yusuf: Diya is not obligatory for the boy or insane person. And al-Shafi'i said to him: No liability is obligatory for any of them, because he killed him in self-defense, so he becomes like a sane adult. This is because he is considered to be compelled to kill him by the latter's act, as if the latter said to him: 'Kill me or I will kill you.' And the fact that the animal is owned by another has no effect on liability, like a slave who draws a sword on a man and kills him; then no liability is obligatory. So this is similar, so it becomes like a slave who attacks a free man and kills him. For Abu Yusuf: Indeed, the act of a boy and an insane person is considered fundamentally, so that it is not considered in respect of obligation of liability, because an animal's injury is free (jubar), and likewise its immunity is for its own right, and the immunity of the animal is for the right of the owner, so their act drops their right by their immunity, so they are not liable. But the animal is liable, unlike game if it attacks a pilgrim (muhrim) or game of the sanctuary upon a non-pilgrim, because the Lawgiver permitted its killing and did not impose upon us bearing its harm. Do you not see that the five noxious animals are permitted to be killed absolutely due to fear of harm from them? So what do you think if harm is actualized and the owner of the animal did not permit? Liability is obligatory. Likewise, the immunity of another's slave is for his own right, and his act is prohibited, so his immunity is dropped by it.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on killing an insane person (majnun) or a boy (sabi) who draws a sword and attacks. The relied-upon Hanafi view is that diya (blood money) is obligatory, not qisas, because these individuals lack full legal capacity (mukallaf) and thus cannot be subject to qisas. The commentary presents two intra-Hanafi positions: (1) The position of Abu Yusuf, who holds that no diya is due because the act of such persons is not legally significant (ghayr mu'tabar) for liability, analogizing them to animals whose injuries are 'jubar' (free from liability). (2) The position attributed to al-Shafi'i, who argues that there is no liability at all because the killing was in self-defense, just as with a sane adult. The Hanafi ruling (mufta bihi) is that diya is wajib, on the basis that the attacker's immunity is not fully extinguished due to diminished capacity, so the defender must pay compensation but is not subject to retaliation. The footnote also discusses animals: if an animal attacks, the owner may be liable, while game in the sanctuary is exempt because the Lawgiver allowed killing it without compensation.

Key Terms
مجنون (majnūn): An insane person lacking legal capacity; killing him requires diya.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a victim when qisas is not applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) Hanafi ruling when a man kills an insane person who draws a sword on him?
A) Qisas is obligatory.
B) No liability.
C) Diya is obligatory.
D) It is permissible without any compensation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, killing an insane or minor attacker requires diya because their immunity is not fully extinguished, but qisas is not applicable due to lack of capacity.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate

Single Act, Multiple Legal Rulings: The Principle of Multiplicity by Effect
Explains that one shot can be two acts, requiring dīyah for unintentional death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a single shot kills two persons (one intentional, one mistaken) and explain the principle that a single physical act can be legally multiple acts due to differing effects.

Core Idea
A single physical act can give rise to multiple legal outcomes when its effects are legally distinct.

The Hanafi school recognizes that a single physical action can carry multiple legal classifications when it produces multiple legally significant effects. This lesson explores a classic case: a hunter shoots at game but the arrow kills two people—one intentionally, one by mistake. The ruling for the mistaken death is wajib diyah (blood money). The legal reasoning is based on the principle that acts are multiplied by their effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The scenario: a single shot kills two persons. The first was intentional (ʿamd), the second was mistaken (khaṭaʾ). The ruling: blood money (diyah) is wajib for the second (mistaken) death only.
The first death may be subject to qisas, but that is not the focus here.
2
Extract the legal principle
The principle invoked is that an act is multiplied by the multiplicity of its effects (al-fiʿl yataʿaddad bi taʿaddud al-athar). The commentator explains that a single release of an arrow is called 'shooting' but depending on the outcome, it can be 'wounding', 'killing', 'breaking', etc.
This principle is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the proof (dalīl ʿaqlī)
The proof is rational: just as a single action can be given different names based on its effects, it can have different legal rulings. The text provides examples to illustrate this linguistic-legal multiplicity.
The proof is not from a textual source but from linguistic usage and legal analogy.
4
Respond to the objection
The objection: 'It is one shot, how can it be multiplied into two different acts?' The response is that the legal classification depends on the effect, not merely the physical act. Thus, the same physical act can be two legal acts if the effects differ legally.
This objection reflects a literalist view that might be held by other schools.
5
Identify the authority level
The passage cites al-Hidāyah and al-Kifāyah, both from the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus. The ruling is muftā bihī and considered reliable in the Hanafi school.
Although some schools may disagree, the Hanafi position is well-established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدية للثاني) ؛ لأنَّ الأول عمد، والثاني خطأ. قوله : والثاني خطأ ؛ أي أحد نوعي الخطأ، كأنه رمى إلى صيد فأصاب آدميّاً والفعل يتعدّد بتعدد الأثر ؛ لأنّ الرمي الواحد جاز أن يتعدَّد بتعدد آثاره ؛ فإنّ الإنسان إذا أرسل سهماً يسمّى رمياً، وإذا فرق جلد حيوان ولم يمت يسمى جرحاً، وإذا أصاب ومات يُسَمَّى قتلاً. وإذا أصاب كوزاً وفرَّقَ تركيبه يسمى كسراً ، وإذا نفذ السهم إلى غير المرمي إليه صار بمنزلة فعل آخر، ولو فيه مخطئ، فيجب الدية، هذا ما في «الهداية» و«الكفاية»، ويندفع بـه مـا يقال : إنه رمى واحداً، فكيف يـتـعـدد ويصير فعـلـيـن متغايرين.
The blood money is for the second) because the first is intentional and the second is mistaken. His saying: 'and the second is mistaken' means one of the two types of mistake, as if he shot at game but hit a human, and the act is multiplied by the multiplicity of its effect; because a single shot can be multiplied by the multiplicity of its effects; for a person, when he releases an arrow, it is called 'shooting', and when it cuts the skin of an animal without killing it, it is called 'wounding', and when it hits and kills, it is called 'killing'. And if it hits a pitcher and breaks its structure, it is called 'breaking', and if the arrow penetrates to something other than the target, it becomes like another act, even if he is mistaken in it, so blood money is obligatory. This is what is in al-Hidāyah and al-Kifāyah, and by this is repelled what is said: 'It is one shot, how can it be multiplied and become two different acts?'
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses a scenario where a single shot kills two persons, one intentionally and one by mistake. The ruling is that blood money (diyah) is due for the second, mistaken death. The principle invoked is that a single physical act can be legally multiple acts if its effects differ in legal classification. The commentary provides examples: releasing an arrow is 'shooting', but if it cuts skin it is 'wounding', if it kills it is 'killing', if it breaks a pot it is 'breaking'. Thus the same act can have multiple legal outcomes. The proof from the Hanafi school is rational (istihsan), based on the multiplicity of effects. The passage cites al-Hidayah and al-Kifayah as sources. It also answers the doubt that one shot cannot be two acts.

Key Terms
عمد (ʿamd): Intentional act, where the perpetrator intends the action and the result (death). In the text, it means deliberate killing with intent and a weapon likely to cause death.
خطأ (khaṭaʾ): Mistaken act, where the perpetrator intended a lawful act but accidentally caused death, e.g., shooting at game hitting a person.
دية (diyyah): Blood money, a financial compensation paid to the heirs for wrongful death, equivalent to a fixed amount (e.g., 100 camels or their monetary value).
تعدد الأثر (taʿaddud al-athar): Multiplicity of effect; the principle that a single act can give rise to multiple legal rulings based on its various outcomes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a case where a single shot kills two persons, one intentionally and one by mistake, what is the ruling regarding the mistaken death?
A) Blood money for both
B) Blood money for the intentional only
C) Blood money for the mistaken only
D) Qisas for both

Key Takeaway
A single physical act can produce multiple legal outcomes; the Hanafi school applies this principle to ensure each death is compensated according to its own legal classification.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate

Hukumat 'Adl for Lash Wounds That Leave a Mark
Ruling on compensation for lash wounds that leave a mark

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that trigger hukumat 'adl versus arsh, and apply the Hanafi principle that mere pain without a permanent mark is not compensable.

Core Idea
A lash wound that leaves a permanent mark requires valuation (hukumat 'adl), not fixed arsh.

This passage from the matn and its commentary clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi diyat law: when does a wound warrant fixed compensation (arsh) and when does it call for a flexible valuation by experts (hukumat 'adl)? The answer hinges on whether the injury leaves a permanent mark. The commentator also draws a sharp boundary: if no wound was inflicted, or if the wound healed completely without a trace, no compensation is due — because mere pain, however severe, is not compensable in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act described? One hundred lashes that wound and leave a mark. The ruling: hukumat 'adl is wajib.
Note the phrase 'wajib' — the obligation is established.
2
Distinguish hukumat from arsh
Why hukumat and not arsh? Because arsh is only for wounds that affect the self (i.e., life-threatening or not healing). Here the wound heals but leaves a mark — so hukumat applies.
arsh considers the effect on the self (nafs); hukumat considers the permanent trace (athar).
3
Trace the negative inference (mafhum mukhalafah)
If no wound was made initially, nothing is due by consensus. If the wound heals completely without a trace, nothing is due according to Abu Hanifa. Why? Because only pain was inflicted.
This is a negative implication: compensation depends on a permanent trace.
4
Recognize the qiyas khafi (hidden analogy)
The commentator compares the healed wound with no mark to a painful blow that leaves no trace. In both cases, only pain is present — and pain alone does not obligate any payment.
This is a silent qiyas: the 'illa (cause) is the absence of a permanent bodily change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتجب حكومة عدل في مئة سوط جرحته وبقي أثرها. قوله : وتجب حكومة عدل؛ دون الأرش؛ لأن حكومة العدل إنما تكون لبقاء الأثر، وهو موجود، والأرش إنما يجب باعتبار الأثر في النفس، بأن لم يبرأ وليس بموجود، وهذا يشير إلى أنه إن لم يكن يجرح في الابتداء لا يجب شيء بالاتفاق وإن جرح واندمل ولم يبق لها أثر فكذلك، كما هو أصل أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه لم يكن إلا مجرد الألم وهو لا يوجب شيئاً كما لو ضرب ضرباً مؤلماً. هكذا في «العناية».
And a government valuation is obligatory for a hundred lashes that wounded it and its effect remained. His statement: 'And a government valuation is obligatory' – without the arsh; because the government valuation is only for the permanence of the effect, and it is present, while the arsh is only obligatory by consideration of the effect on the self, that it did not heal and is not present. And this indicates that if he did not wound initially, nothing is obligatory by agreement, and if he wounded and it healed and no effect remained, likewise, as is the principle of Abu Hanifa; because it was nothing but mere pain, and that does not obligate anything, just as if he struck a painful blow. Thus in al-‘Inaya.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn with its commentary. The ruling states that if a person is lashed one hundred lashes and the wounds leave a permanent mark, then the compensation is a government valuation (hukumat 'adl), not the full arsh. The commentator explains the distinction: hukumat 'adl is due when the effect (trace) remains, while arsh is due only when the injury affects the self (i.e., life) and the wound does not heal. He further clarifies that if no wound was made initially, nothing is due by consensus. Similarly, if the wound healed completely without leaving a trace, nothing is due according to Abu Hanifa because only pain was inflicted, which does not warrant compensation, analogous to a painful blow. This is based on the Hanafi principle that mere pain is not compensable.

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): A form of compensation assessed by two just valuers for injuries that do not have a fixed arsh, when the injury leaves a permanent mark.
أرش (arsh): Fixed compensation for specific injuries, such as the full diyah for loss of a limb or a fraction thereof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What compensation is due for a wound that leaves a permanent mark but does not affect the whole body?
A) Hukumat 'adl
B) Arsh
C) Nothing
D) Qisas

Key Takeaway
A lash wound that leaves a permanent mark requires hukumat 'adl; a wound that heals without a mark warrants no compensation because mere pain is not compensable in Hanafi law.

Forgiveness of Injury Resulting in Death: Accidental vs. Intentional
Ruling on forgiveness of injury including resulting death as a will from one-third or fully

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgiveness of an injury that leads to death, distinguish between accidental and intentional cases, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind the distinction.

Core Idea
Accidental forgiveness is a will from one-third; intentional forgiveness is fully effective because qisas is not property.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the legal effect when a victim forgives an injury that later leads to death. The ruling depends on whether the original injury was accidental or intentional, and the commentary addresses an objection about the killer being an heir, explaining that the forgiveness is a fresh donation, not a bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between accidental (khat') and intentional ('amd) injury leading to death. For accidental, the forgiveness is considered from one-third of the perpetrator's wealth; for intentional, it is fully effective.
The distinction hinges on whether the right is financial (blood-money) or retaliatory (qisas).
2
Analyze the objection
The objection: The killer is one of the 'aqila (tribal sureties) and possibly an heir; a bequest to an heir is invalid. How can the forgiveness be valid? The response: The forgiveness is not a bequest but a fresh donation (tabarru' mubtada'), which is valid for the killer.
The text analogizes to a gift; if the victim gave a gift to the killer and delivered it, it would be valid.
3
Understand the ta'lil for heirs' rights
The text explains that the right of heirs attaches to blood-money (mal) but not to qisas because qisas is not property. The hadith 'For you to leave your heirs wealthy is better...' only applies to wealth, and qisas is not wealth, so the heirs' right does not attach to it.
By analogy, for financial rights, heirs' right attaches only after death, but the hadith accelerates it to protect heirs. For qisas, no such attachment occurs.
4
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, determine whether the forgiveness is limited to one-third (accidental) or fully effective (intentional). Also consider whether the killer is an heir and the effect of the fresh donation argument.
The mufta bihi is that even if the killer is an heir, the forgiveness as a fresh donation is valid for the accidental case up to one-third.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he forgives the injury or the cutting and what results from it, then it is forgiveness for the soul; for accidental homicide from one-third of his wealth, for intentional from all of it. His statement: 'so it is considered from the third... etc.'; if it is said: The killer is one of the 'aqila, so how is it permitted to bequeath a whole third here, even valid for the share of the killer as well, while a bequest is not valid for the killer? We say: That is permitted only because the wounded person did not say: I bequeath to you a third of the blood-money, but rather he forgave the wealth after the cause of obligation, so it was a fresh donation, and that is permissible for the killer. Do you not see that if he gave him something as a gift and delivered it, it is valid? And some said: The amount of the killer's share drops. Thus in al-Kifaya. His statement: 'because the right of the heirs does not attach to it'; because the right of the heirs is only established by way of succession, and the ruling of the substitute is not established while the original exists. And analogically in wealth also, their right would not attach except after the death of the testator. But it is established because of his saying: 'For you to leave your heirs wealthy is better than to leave them poor, begging from people.' And leaving them wealthy is only realized by attaching their right to that which brings wealth, namely wealth. So if their right did not attach, he could dispose of it, leaving them poor begging. And qisas is not wealth, so their right does not attach to it, but it is inherited because inheritance is substitution. Thus in al-‘Inaya.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on forgiveness of injury that leads to death. If a victim forgives the injury (jinaayah) or the cutting and whatever results from it, including death, then this forgiveness is considered a forgiveness of the entire act (the soul). The key distinction: if the original injury was accidental (khat'), then the forgiveness is treated like a will—it is valid only from one-third of the perpetrator's wealth because the heirs have a right to the blood-money, which is a financial right. But if the injury was intentional ('amd), then the forgiveness is effective fully, because the right of the heirs does not attach to qisas (retaliation) as it is not property, so the forgiveness from the victim himself removes the right to qisas completely. The commentary addresses an objection: how can it be valid for the killer to benefit from the bequest when a bequest to the killer is invalid? It explains that this is not a bequest but a fresh donation (tabarru' mubtada'), which is valid. Another point: why does the right of heirs attach to the blood-money but not to qisas? Because qisas is not property, and the hadith about leaving heirs wealthy applies only to wealth.

Key Terms
الجناية (al-jinaayah): The act of injury or aggression, usually resulting in harm; here it refers to the initial injury that may lead to death.
الخطأ (al-khata'): Accidental homicide where the act was not intended to kill.
العمد (al-'amd): Intentional homicide where the act was meant to kill.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will that takes effect after death; here the forgiveness of accidental blood-money is analogized to a wasiyyah from one-third.
تبرع مبتدأ (tabarru' mubtada'): A fresh donation; a gratuitous transfer that is not dependent on a prior obligation or bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The forgiveness is valid only from one-third of the perpetrator's wealth.
B) The forgiveness is fully valid without any limitation.
C) The forgiveness is invalid because the killer cannot benefit from a bequest.
D) The forgiveness requires the consent of the heirs.

Key Takeaway
Forgiveness of an injury leading to death is valid; for accidental cases it is limited to one-third of the victim's wealth (as a bequest), but for intentional cases it is fully effective because qisas is not property.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyat Amounts for Quasi-Intentional and Accidental Killing
Ruling on diya amounts and subdivisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the standard Hanafi diya amounts in gold, silver, and camels, and distinguish between the severe (mghallazah) category for shibh al-amd and the lighter category for khata.

Core Idea
Diya varies: shibh al-amd requires 100 camels in four quarters; khata requires 100 camels in five fifths.

This lesson presents the foundational rulings on diya (blood money) as established in the Hanafi school. The text gives the fixed amounts in gold, silver, and camels, then specifies how these camels are divided for quasi-intentional (shibh al-amd) and accidental (khata) killing. Understanding these categories is essential for distinguishing the severity of liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base diya amounts
The text states the diya in three currencies: 1,000 dinars (gold), 10,000 dirhams (silver), or 100 camels. Note that these are fixed values.
The silver dirhams are of 'weight seven' – 10 dirhams per dinar, consistent with prophetic era standards.
2
Understand the distinction between shibh al-amd and khata
For shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional), the 100 camels are divided into four equal groups of 25, each of a specific age and gender: bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqa, jadha'a. This is called 'severe' (mghallazah). For khata (accidental), the 100 camels are divided into five groups of 20: ibn makhad, ibn labun, hiqqa, jadha'a, and bint makhad.
The difference in the number of categories (4 vs 5) reflects the altered liability: heavier for quasi-intentional, lighter for accidental.
3
Recognize the legal effect of the categories
The severity (mghallazah) for shibh al-amd means the diya is stricter; it must be exacted from the killer's property, and the types of camels are different from khata. In khata, the diya is lighter and often paid by the aqila (tribe/family).
The commentary mentions that texts differ on the exact types; the given list is the Hanafi standard from zahir al-riwayah.

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of al-Wiqaya begins the chapter on diyat. It first states the amounts of blood money (diya) in gold, silver, and camels. Then it categorizes the camels for quasi-intentional (shibh al-amd) killing as four types of twenty-five each (quarters), and for accidental (khata) killing as five types of twenty each (fifths). The following commentary (hashiya) explains the linguistic and legal definitions of diya, notes the equivalence of gold and silver weights from the Prophet's time, and introduces the term 'mghallazah' (severe) indicating that the diya for shibh al-amd is intensified. The discussion follows the Hanafi school's consistent method of defining terms before expounding rulings.

Key Terms
دية (diya): Blood money, the financial compensation paid to the heirs of a person killed by mistake or quasi-intentionally.
شبه العمد (shibh al-amd): Quasi-intentional killing: an act intended but without intent to kill, e.g., hitting with a stick not usually lethal.
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A one-year-old female camel; one of the types of camels used for diya.
مغلظة (mghallazah): Severe or intensified, used to describe the diya for shibh al-amd because of the heavier liability.

Diyat — Blood Money

Definition and Amounts of Diyah in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines diyah and states its amounts for shibh al-amd and khata'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of diyah (blood money) and identify the fixed amounts for quasi-intentional and accidental homicide, including the distinction between aggravated and normal diyah.

Core Idea
Diyah is wajib compensation for life, fixed in gold, silver, or camels, with aggravated (four categories) for shibh al-amd and normal (five categories) for khata'.

This lesson introduces the core of the Hanafi law of diyat (blood money). The passage, drawn from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, defines the term 'diyah' both linguistically and legally, then states the standard amounts payable for quasi-intentional (shibh al-amd) and accidental (khata') homicide. Understanding these fixed categories is essential for applying the law of homicide compensation correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Extract the legal definition of diyah from the commentary: it is the financial substitute for a human life, payable to the victim's heirs. Note that it has become a proper noun for blood money, distinct from 'arsh (compensation for injuries).
The passage cites linguistic sources (al-Mughrib, al-Qamus, al-Sihah) to ground the legal term.
2
State the standard amounts
Memorise the three standard forms: 1,000 gold dinars, 10,000 silver dirhams, or 100 camels. Understand that these amounts are fixed (wajib) in Hanafi law and represent the default compensation.
The gold and silver amounts are based on the Prophet's standard: 1 dinar = 10 dirhams of the weight where 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals.
3
Distinguish between shibh al-amd and khata'
For quasi-intentional homicide (shibh al-amd), the diyah of camels is 'aggravated' (al-mughallazah) and divided into four equal categories (quarters) of 25 each: bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, and jadha'ah. For accidental homicide (khata'), the diyah is divided into five categories (fifths) of 20 each, adding ibn makhad to the previous four.
The aggravation (taghliz) applies only to the camel diyah and only to shibh al-amd; the gold and silver amounts remain the same.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Imam Abu Hanifa restricted diyah to these three types (gold, silver, camels), while his disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allowed cows, sheep, and garments as well. The mufta bihi position permits alternative property.
This ikhtilaf is recorded in later Hanafi works; the default amounts remain the standard.
5
Apply the definition to a scenario
Given a case of accidental killing, identify that the killer's aqila must pay 100 camels (or equivalent) divided into five categories. Recognise that if camels are unavailable, the gold or silver value may be used.
The payment is wajib upon the aqila (tribal insurance pool) for accidental killings.

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Diyat (Blood Money) from the matn. It begins by stating the fixed amounts of diyah: from gold it is 1,000 dinars, from silver 10,000 dirhams, and from camels 100. The passage then specifies that for shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional homicide), the diyah of camels is divided into four categories (quarters), each consisting of 25 camels of a specific age and gender: bint makhad (one-year-old she-camel), bint labun (two-year-old she-camel), hiqqah (three-year-old she-camel), and jadha'ah (four-year-old she-camel). This is called the 'aggravated' diyah (al-mughallazah). For accidental homicide (khata'), the diyah is divided into five categories (fifths) of 20 camels each, including ibn makhad (one-year-old male camel) along with the other four types mentioned. The commentary then explains the linguistic and legal definition of diyah. Linguistically, it is the verbal noun of 'wada' meaning to pay blood money. Legally, it has become a proper noun for the financial compensation paid in lieu of a human life, synonymous with 'arsh (compensation for bodily injuries). The commentator, quoting al-'Inayah, explains the appropriateness of discussing diyat after jinayat (injuries) in legal works, as diyah is one of the consequences of injury, albeit less severe than qisas (retaliation). Finally, it clarifies the standard weight relationship between dinars and dirhams as established in the time of the Prophet: each dinar equals ten dirhams of the weight where ten dirhams equal seven mithqals, as noted in the Book of Zakat.

Key Terms
الدية (al-diyah): The financial compensation paid to the heirs of a homicide victim, fixed in amount and type.
شبه العمد (shibh al-amd): A category of homicide between intentional and accidental, where the killer intended the act but not the death.
المغلظة (al-mughallazah): The aggravated diyah for shibh al-amd, paid in four categories of camels.
الخطأ (khata'): Accidental homicide where the killer had no intent to harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Diyah is wajib blood money fixed at 1,000 dinars, 10,000 dirhams, or 100 camels, with the camel diyah divided into four categories for shibh al-amd and five for khata'.

Types of Property for Diyah: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah payment types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the types of property from which diyah can be paid and explain the evidence of each side.

Core Idea
Diyah can be paid from cows, sheep, and garments according to Sahibayn; Abu Hanifa restricts to gold, silver, and camels.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the types of property from which diyah (blood money) can be paid. While Imam Abu Hanifa limits payment to three specific types, his two companions allow a broader range based on the practice of Caliph Umar. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for knowing the flexibility available in diyah settlements.

Guided Path
1
State the core issue
Identify the legal question: from what types of property can diyah be paid?
The dispute is about types, not amounts.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Abu Hanifa holds that diyah is only from gold, silver, and camels. His evidence is the fixed texts (nusus) that mention only these three.
These three are the 'asl' (original) types.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad add cows, sheep, and garments. Their evidence is the practice of Umar who assigned diyah from the prevalent wealth of each region.
Umar's ruling demonstrates qiyas of suitability.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a killer has no gold/silver/camels, Sahibayn allow direct payment in other forms; Abu Hanifa would require conversion to the three types.
The mufta bihi follows Sahibayn for practicality.

ـتاب الديات / أنواعها وأحكامها
٤٨٥
الدية عند أبي حنيفة له لا تكون إلا من هذه الأموال الثلاثة، وقالا : منها، ومن البقر مئتا بقرة ومن الغنم ألف شاة، ومن الحلل مئتا حلة ، كلُّ حلّةٍ ثوبان ; لأنَّ مر له جعل على أهل كل مال منها.
[٢]
عبارة «الهداية» و«الاختيار» و«الكنز» و «الملتقى» و «تنوير «الابصار» أنّ دية شبه العمد لا تكون إلا من الإبل، وعليه فالتغليظ ظاهراً ; لعدم التخيير.
وظاهر عبارة «الاصلاح» و«الغرر» وغيرها أنها تكون من غير الإبل أيضاً، وإليه مال المصنف له و به صرّح القُدُوري حيث قال : ولا يثبت التغليظُ إلا في الإبل خاصة، فإن قضى من غير الإبل لم تُغلظ. انتهى.
وعليه فمعنى التغليظ فيها أنها إذا وقعت من الإبل تدفع أرباعاً، بخلاف دِية الخطأ، فإنها أخماس ، وفي «المجمع»: تتغلظ دِيَة شبه العمد في الإبل ، قال شارحه : حتى لو قضى بالدية من غير الإبل لم تغلظ ، وكذا في درر البحار وشرحه «غرر الأفكار».
وفي «جنايات» «غاية «البيان»: وتغليظ الدِّيةِ في شبه العمد في الإبل إذا فرضت الدية فيها، فأما غيرُ الإبل فلا يغلظ فيها، وفي «الجوهر»، حتى أنه لا يزداد في الفضة على عشرة آلاف ولا في الذهب على ألف دينار.
وفي «درر البحار»: اتفق الأئمة على أنّ الدِّيَةَ من الذهب في الخطأ وشبه العمد ألف دينار، فهذه العبارات صريحة في أنّ دِيَةَ شبه العمد لا يختص بالإبل. كذا قال الطحطاوي ). [١] قوله : بقرة ... الخ ; وقال الجلبي عن «العناية» (۳) : ويكون قيمة كل بقرة خمسون درهماً، وقيمة كلّ شاة خمسة دراهم وقيمة كلّ حلّة خمسون درهماً، وكلّ
حلة ثوبان : ازار ورداء، وهو المختار، وفي «النهاية»: قيل في زماننا قميص وسراويل. [٢] قوله : لأن عمر جعل على أهل كل مال.... الخ ; قال أبو يوسف له حدثنا
The Book of Diyat / Its Types and Rulings. The blood money according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, is only from these three types of wealth. And the two said: from them, and from cows two hundred cows, and from sheep one thousand sheep, and from garments two hundred garments, each garment being two pieces; because Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, imposed on the people of each wealth from it. [2] The wording of 'al-Hidayah', 'al-Ikhtiyar', 'al-Kanz', 'al-Multaqa', and 'Tanwir al-Absar' is that the diyah of quasi-intentional homicide is only from camels, and accordingly the aggravation is apparent due to the lack of choice. And the apparent wording of 'al-Islah', 'al-Ghurar', and others is that it can be from other than camels as well, and the author inclined to it, and al-Quduri stated it explicitly where he said: And aggravation is established only with camels specifically, so if he judged by other than camels, it is not aggravated. End. And accordingly, the meaning of aggravation in it is that when it occurs from camels, it is paid in quarters, unlike the diyah of accident, for it is in fifths. And in 'al-Majma': The diyah of quasi-intentional homicide is aggravated with camels. Its commentator said: Even if he judged by diyah from other than camels, it is not aggravated. Similarly in 'Durar al-Bihar' and its commentary 'Ghurar al-Afkar'. And in 'Jinayat Ghayat al-Bayan': And the aggravation of diyah in quasi-intentional homicide is with camels when the diyah is imposed in them; as for other than camels, it is not aggravated in them. And in 'al-Jawhar', even that it is not increased in silver over ten thousand nor in gold over one thousand dinars. And in 'Durar al-Bihar': The imams agreed that the diyah from gold in accidental and quasi-intentional homicide is one thousand dinars. So these statements are explicit that the diyah of quasi-intentional homicide is not specific to camels. Thus said al-Tahtawi. [1] His saying: cows...etc. And al-Jalabi said from 'al-Inayah': And the value of each cow is fifty dirhams, and the value of each sheep is five dirhams, and the value of each garment is fifty dirhams, and each garment is two pieces: a waist wrap and a cloak, and that is the chosen. And in 'al-Nihayah': It was said in our time: a shirt and trousers. [2] His saying: Because Umar imposed on the people of each wealth...etc. Abu Yusuf said to us: He narrated...
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the types of wealth from which diyah can be paid. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, diyah is restricted to the three types mentioned previously: gold (1000 dinars), silver (10,000 dirhams), and camels (100). However, his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), hold that diyah can also be paid from cows (200 cows), sheep (1000 sheep), or garments (200 garments, each consisting of two pieces). Their evidence is the practice of Caliph Umar, who assigned diyah to the people of each region according to their prevalent wealth. The passage then discusses a related issue: whether the taghliz (aggravation) of diyah for shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional homicide) applies only when the diyah is paid in camels. According to the majority of Hanafi texts like al-Hidayah, al-Ikhtiyar, etc., diyah for shibh al-amd is exclusively from camels, so taghliz naturally applies. However, according to al-Islah, al-Ghurar, and others, diyah can be from other sources as well, and taghliz only applies when it is paid in camels. Al-Quduri explicitly states that if a judge awards diyah from other than camels, no taghliz applies. The commentator reconciles by explaining that taghliz means paying in four categories (quarters) when from camels, whereas accidental diyah is paid in five categories (fifths). Later sources like al-Majma', Durar al-Bihar, and Ghayat al-Bayan affirm that taghliz is specific to camels, and if diyah is paid from gold or silver, the amounts remain the same (1000 dinars or 10,000 dirhams) without increase. The passage concludes with a note on the valuation of cows, sheep, and garments: each cow is valued at 50 dirhams, each sheep at 5 dirhams, and each garment at 50 dirhams, with the garment consisting of two pieces (e.g., izār and ridā', or in later times a shirt and trousers). This thoroughly explains the Hanafi position on the flexibility of diyah payment forms while maintaining the principle of taghliz only for camel diyah.

Key Terms
الحلل (al-hulal): Garments, specifically two-piece suits (each hullah is a set of two garments).
الثلاثة (al-thalatha): The three types: gold, silver, and camels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the source text, what is the evidence for the Sahibayn's position that diyah can be paid from cows, sheep, and garments?
A) A hadith from the Prophet
B) The practice of Caliph Umar
C) Qiyas on gold
D) Ijma of the Sahaba

Key Takeaway
Diyah can be paid from cows, sheep, and garments according to the Sahibayn, and this is the mufta bihi.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Taghliz (Aggravation) of Diyah in Shibh al-Amd
Discussion of taghliz condition in diyah for shibh al-amd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on taghliz (aggravation) of diyah in quasi-intentional homicide and identify when taghliz applies.

Core Idea
Taghliz of diyah applies only when paid in camels; if paid from other types, no aggravation.

This lesson focuses on the concept of taghliz (aggravation) in diyah for shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional homicide). The Hanafi school is unanimous that taghliz only applies when diyah is paid in camels, not when paid from gold, silver, or other property. Understanding this is crucial for judges and scholars to properly apply the aggravated form of compensation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of taghliz
Taghliz in diyah means paying the 100 camels in four categories (arba') of 25 each, as opposed to accidental diyah which is in five categories (akhamas).
The aggravation is in the mode of payment, not the total number.
2
Identify the condition for taghliz
According to the majority of Hanafi texts, taghliz only applies when the diyah is actually paid in camels.
The key phrase: 'لا يثبت التغليظ إلا في الإبل خاصة'
3
Examine the alternative view
Some texts (al-Islah, al-Ghurar) allow diyah for shibh al-amd from non-camel sources, but then no taghliz applies.
Al-Quduri explicitly states: if judge awards from other than camels, it is not aggravated.
4
Confirm the consensus on taghliz condition
Sources like al-Majma', Durar al-Bihar, and Ghayat al-Bayan affirm that taghliz is specific to camels.
Even in gold or silver, the amounts remain the same without increase.

Commentary

This thoroughly explains the Hanafi position on the flexibility of diyah payment forms while maintaining the principle of taghliz only for camel diyah.

Key Terms
التغليظ (al-taghliz): The aggravation of diyah for shibh al-amd by paying in four categories (quarters) of camels.
شبه العمد (shibh al-amd): Quasi-intentional homicide: intentional act but with an object meant for striking, not killing, or other factors that reduce culpability.
أرباع (arba'): Four: the diyah is divided into four groups of 25 camels each.

Key Takeaway
Taghliz of diyah for shibh al-amd is only applicable when the payment is made in camels, not in gold, silver, or other property.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyat Types, Taghliz, and the Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Silver Amount
Combined intra- and inter-madhhab analysis of diyat types and shibh al-amd taghliz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on diyat types, explain the aggravation of diyat in shibh al-amd, and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute over the amount of diyat in silver.

Core Idea
Diyat for shibh al-amd is aggravated only when paid in camels; the Hanafi amount in silver is 10,000 dirhams, contra Shafi'i's 12,000.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on diyat (blood money), focusing on intra-Hanafi differences regarding the types of property from which diyat may be paid, the special aggravation (taghliz) for quasi-intentional homicide (shibh al-amd), and the inter-madhhab disagreement over the amount in silver. We will work through the proofs and reasoning to understand the operative positions in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is paying diyat. Determine the hukm level (wajib) and note that the details vary by type of homicide and school.
Diyat is wajib on the perpetrator or his 'aqila.
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on property types
Compare Abu Hanifa's view (only camels, gold, silver) with the Sahibayn's view (also cows, sheep, suits). Identify the proof from Umar's practice.
The Sahibayn relied on a narration of Umar assigning diyat to each type.
3
Analyze the disagreement on shibh al-amd taghliz
Note that some Hanafi texts restrict diyat for shibh al-amd to camels, while others allow alternatives but limit aggravation to camels. Identify the ruling of al-Quduri and the author's inclination.
Taghliz means paying in fours (not fifths) and only applies when camels are used.
4
Understand the aggravated diyat composition
When diyat is paid in camels with taghliz, it consists of 75 camels in three age categories: 25 bint makhad, 25 bint labun, 25 hiqqah. Contrast with the five categories for khata'.
The ages ensure fair value distribution.
5
Evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute on silver amount
Hanafi holds 10,000 dirhams (from hadith of Ibn Umar); Shafi'i and Maliki hold 12,000 (from hadith of Ibn Abbas). Understand the Hanafi response: preferring the lesser amount for certainty, or interpreting the other hadith differently.
This difference has practical implications for diyat payments.

الدية عند أبي حنيفة له لا تكون إلا من هذه الأموال الثلاثة، وقالا : منها، ومن البقر مئتا بقرة ومن الغنم ألف شاة، ومن الحلل مئتا حلة ، كلُّ حلّةٍ ثوبان ؛ لأنَّ مر له جعل على أهل كل مال منها.
[١] قوله : بقرة ... الخ ؛ وقال الجلبي عن «العناية» (۳) : ويكون قيمة كل بقرة خمسون درهماً، وقيمة كلّ شاة خمسة دراهم وقيمة كلّ حلّة خمسون درهماً، وكلّ حلّة ثوبان : ازار ورداء، وهو المختار، وفي «النهاية»: قيل في زماننا قميص وسراويل.

عبارة «الهداية» و«الاختيار» و«الكنز» و «الملتقى» و «تنوير «الابصار» أنّ دية شبه العمد لا تكون إلا من الإبل، وعليه فالتغليظ ظاهراً ؛ لعدم التخيير.

وعليه فمعنى التغليظ فيها أنها إذا وقعت من الإبل تدفع أرباعاً، بخلاف دِية الخطأ، فإنها أخماس ، وفي «المجمع»: تتغلظ دِيَة شبه العمد في الإبل ، قال شارحه : حتى لو قضى بالدية من غير الإبل لم تغلظ ، وكذا في درر البحار وشرحه «غرر الأفكار».
وفي «جنايات» «غاية «البيان»: وتغليظ الدِّيةِ في شبه العمد في الإبل إذا فرضت الدية فيها، فأما غيرُ الإبل فلا يغلظ فيها، وفي «الجوهر»، حتى أنه لا يزداد في الفضة على عشرة آلاف ولا في الذهب على ألف دينار.
وفي «درر البحار»: اتفق الأئمة على أنّ الدِّيَةَ من الذهب في الخطأ وشبه العمد ألف دينار، فهذه العبارات صريحة في أنّ دِيَةَ شبه العمد لا يختص بالإبل. كذا قال الطحطاوي ).
ثمَّ الدِّية المغلظة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف : خمس وعشرون بنت مخاض : وهي التي تمت عليها حول، وخمس وعشرون بنت لبون : وهي التي تمت عليها حولان وخمس وعشرون حقة : وهي التي تمت عليها ثلاث سنين
إن هذه الأشياء مجهولة ، فلا يصح بها التقدير، ولم يرد فيها أثر مشهور بخلاف
الإبل، وعند الشافعي : من الورق اثنا عشر ألف درهم.
والجواب عن قضاء عمر الله أنه يحتمل أن عمره إنّما قضى بذلك لطريق الصلح بعدما قضى بالدراهم أو الدنانير، إذ الصلح من الدِّية على مال آخر جائز. كذا في «الكفاية»(۳).
وعند الشافعي : وهو قول مالك لما رويا عن ابن عباس أن رجلا قتل فجعل النبي المدينه اثنا عشر ألفا رواه أبو داود والترمذي ؛ ولأنه لاختلاف أنها من الدنانير ألف دينار، وكانت قيمة الدينار على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اثنا عشر درهماً.
لنا : وروي عن ابن - عمر : إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى بالدية في قتيل بعشرة آلاف درهم، وما قلنا أولى ؛ للتيقن به ؛ لأنه أقلّ، أو يحملُ ما روياه على وزن خمسة وما
Book of Diyat / Types and Rulings. According to Abu Hanifa, diyah is not from except these three types of property. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: from them, and from cows: two hundred cows, and from sheep: one thousand sheep, and from suits: two hundred suits, each suit being two garments; because Umar placed on each people of property from it. [1] His saying: cow... etc.; and al-Jalabi from al-Inayah: the value of each cow is fifty dirhams, and the value of each sheep is five dirhams, and the value of each suit is fifty dirhams, and each suit is two garments: a loincloth and a mantle, which is the chosen; and in al-Nihayah: it is said in our time a shirt and trousers. [2] His saying: because Umar placed on each people of property... etc.; Abu Yusuf narrated to us from Ibn Abi Layla from al-Sha'bi from Ubaydah al-Salaqi that Umar ibn al-Khattab placed diyat on the people of gold: one thousand dinars, and on the people of silver: ten thousand dirhams, and on the people of camels: one hundred camels, and on the people of cows: two hundred cows, and on the people of sheep: two thousand sheep, and on the people of suits: two hundred suits. Thus in al-Inayah. The expression of al-Hidayah, al-Ikhtiyar, al-Kanz, al-Multaqa, and Tanwir al-Absar: that diyat of shibh al-amd is only from camels, and accordingly the aggravation is apparent, due to lack of choice. And the apparent expression of al-Islah, al-Ghurrar and others is that it is also from other than camels; and the author inclined to this, and al-Quduri explicitly stated: aggravation is only established in camels particularly, and if he decrees from other than camels, it is not aggravated. End. And accordingly the meaning of aggravation therein is that when it is from camels, it is paid in fourths, unlike diyat of error which is in fifths. And in al-Majma': diyat of shibh al-amd is aggravated in camels. Its commentator said: so if he decrees diyya from other than camels, it is not aggravated. Similarly in Durar al-Bihar and its commentary Ghurar al-Afkar. And in Jina'at of Ghayat al-Bayan: aggravation of diyya in shibh al-amd is in camels when diyya is assessed in them; as for other than camels, it is not aggravated therein. And in al-Jawhar: so that it is not increased in silver beyond ten thousand nor in gold beyond one thousand dinars. And in Durar al-Bihar: the imams agreed that diyya from gold in error and shibh al-amd is one thousand dinars. These expressions are explicit that diyat of shibh al-amd is not restricted to camels. Thus said al-Tahtawi. Then the aggravated diyah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: twenty-five bint makhad—which has completed one year; twenty-five bint labun—which has completed two years; twenty-five hiqqah—which has completed three years. These things are unknown, so estimation through them is not valid, and there is no well-known tradition about them, unlike camels. And according to al-Shafi'i: from silver, twelve thousand dirhams. And the answer about Umar's decree: it is possible that Umar decreed that by way of reconciliation after he had decreed dirhams or dinars, because reconciliation from diyya for other property is permissible. Thus in al-Kifayah. And according to al-Shafi'i—and it is the saying of Malik—because they narrated from Ibn Abbas that a man was killed and the Prophet decreed twelve thousand—narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi; and because it is different that it is from dinars one thousand, and the value of a dinar in the time of the Prophet was twelve dirhams. Our proof: it is narrated from Ibn Umar that the Prophet decreed diyya for a killed man as ten thousand dirhams, and what we say is more appropriate due to certainty, because it is less, or the narration they reported may be interpreted as the weight of five and...
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah and addresses several issues regarding diyat (blood money). It opens with an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that diyat is only from three types of property—camels, gold, and silver—whereas Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) add cows, sheep, and suits (hullal). The Sahibayn base their view on a narration from Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) who assigned diyat in multiples of these items. The commentators then specify the values: a cow equals fifty dirhams, a sheep five dirhams, and a suit fifty dirhams. The suit consists of two garments: traditionally an izār (loincloth) and a ridā’ (mantle), but in modern terms a shirt and trousers. The text then moves to the diyat for shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional homicide). There is a difference among Hanafi scholars: the majority (Hidayah, Ikhtiyar, Kanz, Multaqa, Tanwir al-Absar) state that diyat for shibh al-amd must be in camels alone, hence the aggravation (taghlīẓ) is automatic. However, another group (Islah, Ghurar, and al-Quduri) hold that diyat may be paid from other commodities, and aggravation only applies when camels are used. The author of this commentary seems to favour the latter view. The aggravation means that the camels are paid in four installments, as opposed to the five installments for khata’ (accidental homicide). The text also quotes that all imams agree that diyat from gold is one thousand dinars for both error and shibh al-amd. Then the passage discusses the specific number of camels in the aggravated diyat: twenty-five bint makhad (one-year-olds), twenty-five bint labun (two-year-olds), and twenty-five hiqqah (three-year-olds). A refutation is given against the use of cows, sheep, and suits as standards because their values are uncertain and no well-known tradition (athar mashhur) supports them, unlike camels. The narration from Umar is reinterpreted as a reconciliation (sulh) after a dirham/dinar verdict, not a primary ruling. Finally, the Shafi'i view is presented: diyat from silver is twelve thousand dirhams, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi response cites a hadith from Ibn Umar setting diyat at ten thousand dirhams, arguing that the lesser amount is more certain, or that the other narration refers to the weight of five [dirhams?]. Throughout, the commentary maintains Hanafi methodology, preferring istihsan and reliable transmitted reports.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a homicide victim.
شبه العمد (shibh al-amd): Quasi-intentional homicide: unjustified striking with no intent to kill but using a lethal means.
تغليظ (taghliz): Aggravation of diyat in shibh al-amd, meaning payment in fours instead of fifths, and only in camels.
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): Female camel that has completed one year and entered the second.
بنت لبون (bint labun): Female camel that has completed two years and entered the third.
حقة (hiqqah): Female camel that has completed three years and entered the fourth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi position on the amount of diyat in silver for shibh al-amd?
A) 12,000 dirhams
B) 10,000 dirhams
C) 1,000 dinars
D) 200 cows

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that diyat for shibh al-amd is not restricted to camels, but aggravation (taghliz) only applies when camels are used; the amount in silver is 10,000 dirhams.

Invalidity of Estimation with Unknown Items
Commentary on why unknown items cannot be used for diyah estimation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on estimating diyah with unknown items and explain how Caliph Umar's practice is reconciled via sulh.

Core Idea
Estimation of diyah requires items of known value; unknown items cannot be used, and Umar's apparent counterexample is explained as a sulh.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya clarifies a key Hanafi principle in diyat: the estimation (taqdir) of blood money must be based on items with known monetary value. The commentator addresses an apparent conflict from Caliph Umar's judgments and resolves it through the concept of sulh (reconciliation). Understanding this ruling helps avoid misapplying historical precedents that were based on compromise rather than the original obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The matn states that certain items are 'unknown' and estimation with them is invalid. Recognize that this is a prohibition against using items without clear market value.
The ruling is about the method of determining diyah, not about the permissibility of the items themselves.
2
Understand the basis
Commentary explains: estimation requires known monetary value and a well-known tradition. Unknown items lack both, so they cannot ground a legally enforceable obligation.
Known value ensures certainty; tradition ensures acceptance (e.g., camels are established).
3
Recognize the counter-evidence
Caliph Umar reportedly fixed diyah using various livestock. This might seem to contradict the ruling, as items like cows have known value but lack a strong textual precedent.
The objection is that Umar's practice could be used to legitimize any item with known value.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The commentator resolves this: Umar's judgment was a form of sulh (reconciliation) after he had determined the diyah in standard currency (dirhams/dinars). Sulh on diyah to other property is permissible, but it does not change the original rule.
Thus, Umar's action does not serve as a proof for using unknown items as the primary basis for estimation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن هذه الأشياء مجهولة ، فلا يصح بها التقدير، ولم يرد فيها أثر مشهور بخلاف الإبل. [١] قوله : إنّ هذه الأشياء مجهولة... الخ ؛ توضيحه : إن التقدير إنما يستقيم بشيء معلوم المالية، وهذه الأشياء مجهولة المالية ؛ ولذا لا يقيد بهذه الأشياء ضمان ولم يرد فيها أثر مشهور، بخلاف الإبل. والجواب عن قضاء عمر الله أنه يحتمل أن عمره إنّما قضى بذلك لطريق الصلح بعدما قضى بالدراهم أو الدنانير، إذ الصلح من الدِّية على مال آخر جائز. كذا في «الكفاية»(۳).
These things are unknown, so estimation with them is not valid, and no well-known tradition has been reported regarding them, unlike camels. [1] His statement: 'These things are unknown... etc.'; its clarification: Estimation is correct only with something of known monetary value, and these things are of unknown monetary value; therefore, guarantee is not bound by these things, and no well-known tradition has been reported regarding them, unlike camels. And the answer regarding the judgment of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) is that it is probable that Umar only judged by that as a way of reconciliation after he had judged with dirhams or dinars, since reconciliation from diyah to other property is permissible. As stated in 'Al-Kifayah'.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from the matn (likely from Nur al-Idah) that certain items are 'unknown' and thus cannot be used to estimate diyah. The commentator clarifies that for estimation to be valid, the item must have a known monetary value. These items lack that, and no widely known hadith supports their use, unlike camels which have well-established rulings. The commentator also addresses an objection from the practice of Caliph Umar, who reportedly fixed diyah using various items (camels, cows, sheep, etc.). The response is that Umar's judgment was likely a form of sulh (reconciliation) after he had already determined the diyah in dirhams or dinars, as sulh on diyah for other property is permissible. This shows the Hanafi principle that the basic obligation is in dirhams/dinars, and other items can be accepted via compromise.

Key Terms
تقدير (taqdir): Estimation of monetary value for diyah purposes.
صلح (sulh): A legal compromise or settlement, here allowing diyah to be paid in items other than the standard currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) They are prohibited in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Estimation of diyah requires items of known monetary value and textual precedent; any deviation is invalid unless accepted via sulh after the obligation is fixed in standard currency.

Reconciling the Diyah Narrations: 10,000 vs 12,000 Dirhams
Inter-madhhab dispute with historical-reconciliation analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi reconciliation of the 10,000 vs 12,000 dirham diyah narrations and evaluate the reasoning using historical dirham weight standards.

Core Idea
The Hanafi diyah of 10,000 dirhams equals the Shafi'i 12,000 when dirham weight differences are accounted for.

This lesson examines a well-known inter-madhhab dispute concerning the amount of diyah (blood money) in dirhams. The Shafi'i school, following a hadith from Ibn Abbas and a gold-to-silver conversion, sets diyah at 12,000 dirhams, while the Hanafi school, relying on a hadith from Ibn Umar, sets it at 10,000. Rather than a contradiction, the Hanafis reconcile the two narrations by considering the historical variation in dirham weight standards. Understanding this reconciliation reveals a deeper method of harmonizing conflicting textual evidence and provides insight into Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing positions and their proofs
Read the source text to determine the Hanafi position (10,000 dirhams) and the Shafi'i/Maliki position (12,000 dirhams). Note the hadith each school cites: Ibn Umar for Hanafis, Ibn Abbas for Shafi'is.
This step establishes the prima facie contradiction.
2
Analyze the Hanafi argument for certainty (al-yaqin)
The text says the Hanafi position is 'awla' (preferable) because it gives the lesser amount, bringing certainty. Reflect on the principle that the lesser obligation is preferred when there is doubt.
This is a usul al-fiqh principle: al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk.
3
Understand the dirham weight system
Study the three categories of dirhams: wazn 'asharah (10 dirhams = 10 dinars), wazn sittah (10 dirhams = 6 dinars), wazn khamsah (10 dirhams = 5 dinars). Learn that Caliph Umar later standardized by mixing them.
This historical context is key to the reconciliation.
4
Trace the reconciliation calculation
The Hanafi argument: if the Shafi'i 12,000 dirhams are of the wazn khamsah type (each dirham = 0.5 dinar equivalent) and the Hanafi 10,000 dirhams are of the wazn sittah type (each = 0.6 dinar equivalent), the total silver weight is equal. Verify mathematically: 12,000 * 5/10 = 6,000 dinar worth; 10,000 * 6/10 = 6,000 dinar worth.
Thus the conflict is only apparent, not real.
5
Evaluate the thamarah (practical difference)
In practice, the Hanafi school holds diyah at 10,000 dirhams (or 1,000 dinars), while Shafi'i holds at 12,000 dirhams. However, if the actual silver weight is standardised, the compensation may be equivalent. The difference remains in the counting unit, which can affect payment if dirham types are specified.
This shows how ikhtilaf may have minimal practical impact when context is accounted for.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢] قوله : وعند الشافعي ؛ وهو قول مالك لما رويا عن ابن عباس أن رجلا قتل فجعل النبي المدينة اثنا عشر ألفا رواه أبو داود والترمذي ؛ ولأنه لاختلاف أنها من الدنانير ألف دينار، وكانت قيمة الدينار على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اثنا عشر درهماً. لنا : وروي عن ابن عمر : إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى بالدية في قتيل بعشرة آلاف درهم، وما قلنا أولى ؛ للتيقن به ؛ لأنه أقلّ، أو يحملُ ما روياه على وزن خمسة وما رويناه على وزن سنّة [؟] ; لأنّ الدراهم كانت مختلفة من عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى عهد عمر على ثلاث مراتب : الأول : وزن عشرة : أي العشرة منه وزن عشرة دنانير وهو قدر الدينار. والثاني : وزن ستة ؛ أي العشرة منه وزن ستة. والثالث وزن خمسة ؛ أي كل عشرة منه وزن خمسة من الدنانير. فوقع التنازع بين الناس في الإيفاء والاستيفاء، فجمع عمر له بين الثلاثة فخلط فجعله ثلاثة دراهم، فصار ثلث المجموع درهماً، ولما كان الدينار عشرون قيراطاً، فوزنُ العشرة يكون مثله عشرون قيراطاً ضرورة استوائهما، ووزن الستة يكون نصف الدينار وعشرة فيكون اثنى عشر قيراطاً، ووزن الخمسة يكون نصف الدينار فيكون عشرة قراريط. فيكون المجموع اثنين وأربعين قيراطاً ; فإن جعلتها أثلاثاً صار كل ثلث أربعة عشر قيراطاً، والقيراط خمس شعيرات، وهو الذي كانت عليه دراهمهم، فإذا حمل ما رواه الشافعي له على وزن خمسة، وما روينا على وزن ستة استويا.
[2] His statement: And according to al-Shafi'i; and it is the saying of Malik because they narrated from Ibn Abbas that a man was killed and the Prophet (peace be upon him) set it at twelve thousand in Medina, narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi; and because it is [based on the opinion] that it (diyah) is one thousand dinars, and the value of a dinar at the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was twelve dirhams. Our proof: It is narrated from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged diyah for a slain person as ten thousand dirhams, and what we say is preferable because of certainty, as it is the lesser, or their narration is carried upon the weight of five, and our narration upon the weight of six; because dirhams were different from the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to the time of Umar upon three categories: First: weight of ten, i.e., ten of them weigh ten dinars, which is the weight of a dinar. Second: weight of six, i.e., ten of them weigh six. Third: weight of five, i.e., every ten of them weigh five dinars. Then dispute occurred among people regarding fulfillment and receipt, so Umar combined the three and mixed them and made them three dirhams, so one third of the total became a dirham. And since the dinar is twenty qirats, the weight of ten is likewise twenty qirats necessarily because of equality, and the weight of six is half a dinar and ten, so it becomes twelve qirats, and the weight of five is half a dinar, so it becomes ten qirats. Thus the total becomes forty-two qirats; if you divide it into thirds, each third becomes fourteen qirats, and the qirat is five hairs, and that is what their dirhams were upon. So if the narration of al-Shafi'i is carried upon the weight of five, and our narration upon the weight of six, they become equal.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the amount of diyah in dirhams. The Shafi'i school (and also Imam Malik) holds that diyah is 12,000 dirhams, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) set it at twelve thousand in Medina. They also reason that diyah in gold is 1,000 dinars, and at the Prophet's time a dinar was worth 12 dirhams, so 1,000 x 12 = 12,000. The Hanafi school responds with a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet set diyah at 10,000 dirhams. The Hanafis argue that their position is preferable because it gives the lesser amount, which brings certainty. To reconcile the two narrations, the Hanafis note that different dirham weights existed. They explain that dirhams during the Prophet's time and later varied: some were of 'weight ten' (10 dirhams = 10 dinars), some 'weight six' (10 dirhams = 6 dinars), some 'weight five' (10 dirhams = 5 dinars). Caliph Umar later standardized the dirham by mixing these three types, making an average. The calculation shows that if the Shafi'i's 12,000 dirhams are of the 'weight five' type, and the Hanafi's 10,000 dirhams are of the 'weight six' type, the actual silver weight becomes equal. Thus, there is no real contradiction; the difference is only in the counting unit, not the actual value. This reconciliation shows the Hanafi method of harmonizing conflicting hadith through historical context.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the family of a homicide victim.
وزن ستة (wazn sittah): A dirham weight where 10 dirhams weigh 6 dinars (i.e., 0.6 dinar each).
وزن خمسة (wazn khamsah): A dirham weight where 10 dirhams weigh 5 dinars (i.e., 0.5 dinar each).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi reconciliation, how is the Shafi'i's 12,000 dirham diyah made equivalent to the Hanafi's 10,000 dirham diyah?
A) By considering that the 12,000 dirhams are from the 'weight six' type.
B) By considering that the 12,000 dirhams are from the 'weight five' type and the 10,000 from the 'weight six' type.
C) By dividing both amounts by 1.2.
D) The numbers are not equivalent; the Hanafis reject the 12,000 hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis reconcile the diyah narrations by proving that 10,000 heavier dirhams equal 12,000 lighter dirhams in silver value, thus harmonising the sunnah.
