Camel Types and Ages for Heavy Diyah – Hanafi Positions
Classification of camels for heavy diyah with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the types and ages of camels for heavy diyah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
For heavy diyah, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf require equal numbers of four camel ages; Muhammad requires three ages, all pregnant.

Heavy diyah (al-diyah al-mughallazah) is a severe form of blood money required in cases such as willful homicide. The Hanafi school has internal differences regarding the exact composition of the 100 camels to be paid. In this lesson, we examine the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, noting the practical implications for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the heavy diyah is a wajib obligation of 100 camels, imposed in specific homicide cases. Its composition is the subject of ikhtilaf.
The ruling is drawn from general principles of diyat.
2
List the four types according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
According to the majority Hanafi view, the 100 camels are divided equally: 25 bint makhad (1-year-old), 25 bint labun (2-year-old), 25 hiqqah (3-year-old), and 25 jadha'ah (4-year-old).
No pregnancy requirement.
3
List Muhammad al-Shaybani's alternative
Muhammad, also followed by al-Shafi'i, divides the 100 camels as: 30 hiqqah, 30 jadha'ah, and 40 thaniyyah (5-year-old), all of which must be pregnant (khalfah) with a fetus of at least six months.
This view adds a higher age and a pregnancy condition.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference lies in which exact camels are to be paid—different ages and the presence of pregnancy—affecting valuation and availability.
The dispute affects both intra-Hanafi practice and inter-madhhab comparison.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it is the majority view within the school and is presented first in the text.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمَّ الدِّية المغلظة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف : خمس وعشرون بنت مخاض : وهي التي تمت عليها حول، وخمس وعشرون بنت لبون : وهي التي تمت عليها حولان وخمس وعشرون حقة : وهي التي تمت عليها ثلاث سنين، وخمس وعشرون جذعة : وهي التي تمت عليها أربع سنين، وعند محمد والشافعي (١) ثلاثون حقة، وثلاثون جدعة، وأربعونَ ثنية كلها خَلِفَاتِ في بطونها أولادها الثنية : التي تمت عليها خمس سنين، والخَلِفَة : التي في بطنها ولد مضت عليه سنة أشهر.
Then the heavy diyah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is: twenty-five bint makhad (she-camel that has completed one year), and twenty-five bint labun (she-camel that has completed two years), and twenty-five hiqqah (she-camel that has completed three years), and twenty-five jadha'ah (she-camel that has completed four years). And according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i: thirty hiqqah, thirty jadha'ah, and forty thiniyyah, all of them khalfat (pregnant she-camels with offspring in their wombs). Ath-thiniyyah: she-camel that has completed five years. Al-khalfah: she-camel that has an offspring in her womb that has passed six months.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage details the types and ages of camels required for the heavy diyah (diyah maghlazah) in cases of willful homicide or similar. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the 100 camels are divided equally into four categories of 25 each: bint makhad (one-year-old), bint labun (two-year-old), hiqqah (three-year-old), and jadha'ah (four-year-old). According to Muhammad al-Shaybani (and also Imam al-Shafi'i), the distribution is different: 30 hiqqah (three-year-olds), 30 jadha'ah (four-year-olds), and 40 thiniyyah (five-year-olds), and all these must be pregnant (khalfah) with offspring that have completed six months in the womb. The definitions of thiniyyah (five-year-old) and khalfah (pregnant with a fetus of at least six months) are given. This difference is an intra-Hanafi dispute (between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and also an inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i. The Hanafi school relies on the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf for fatwa, as it is the majority view within the school.

Key Terms
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A female camel that has completed one year and entered its second year.
جذعة (jadh'ah): A female camel that has completed four years and entered its fifth year.
ثنية (thaniyyah): A female camel that has completed five years and entered its sixth year.
خلفة (khalfah): A pregnant she-camel, specifically with a fetus that has passed six months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, how many of the 100 camels for heavy diyah should be hiqqah (three-year-olds)?
A) 20
B) 25
C) 30
D) 40

Key Takeaway
The heavy diyah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf requires 25 each of bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, and jadha'ah; Muhammad's alternative distribution includes pregnancy and a fifth age.

The Sahaba Dispute on Aggravation of Diyah and the Hanafi Choice
Statement of disagreement and school choice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the aggravation of diyah and explain why the school follows Ibn Mas'ud's view among the Companions.

Core Idea
Taghliz of diyah was disputed among Sahaba; Hanafis adopted Ibn Mas'ud's ruling.

The Hanafi school often bases its rulings on the opinions of senior Companions, especially those known for deep legal acumen. In the case of diyah aggravation (taghliz), the Companions themselves differed. This short passage identifies that difference and reveals the Hanafi choice: the view of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Understanding why a particular Companion's view is preferred gives insight into Hanafi methodology of weighting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The text mentions 'taghliz' (aggravation) of diyah. This refers to the additional requirements that make the blood money heavier, such as using specific types of camels or applying it in certain circumstances (e.g., intentional killing, sacred months).
Taghliz is a sub‑rule within the law of diyat.
2
Recognize the dispute among the Sahaba
The passage explicitly states that taghliz was 'different fīhi bayn al‐ṣaḥābah' — a matter of disagreement among the Companions. This indicates that there was no single agreed view from the prophetic era; multiple opinions existed.
The text does not list the differing views, only that they existed.
3
Identify the Hanafi choice
The Hanafi school says 'wa naḥnu akhadhnā bi qawl Ibn Masʿūd' — we have taken the saying of Ibn Mas'ud. This means that among the various Companion opinions, the Hanafis give preference to Ibn Mas'ud's view on taghliz.
Ibn Mas'ud was a prominent Companion and a major source of Hanafi fiqh through the Kufan school.
4
Understand the significance of following a Companion's view
In Hanafi usul, the qawl of a Companion is a source of law (masdar min masādir al‐tashrīʿ) when there is no clear text from Quran or Sunnah, especially if the Companion is known for legal reasoning. This passage illustrates that practice.
Other schools may follow different Companions or rely on other evidence.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
In modern cases of qisas/diyat, the Hanafi mufti will apply the rules of taghliz as transmitted from Ibn Mas'ud. For example, the specific camels required for maghlazah diyah are those prescribed in the ḥadīth and interpreted by Ibn Mas'ud.
The exact details of Ibn Mas'ud's view are elaborated in other texts; this passage only establishes the source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتغليظُ مختلف فيه بين الصحابة ، ونحنُ أخذنا بقول ابن مسعود .
And the aggravation (tashdid) is disputed among the Companions, and we have adopted the saying of Ibn Mas'ud.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This short passage states that the ruling regarding the aggravation (tashdid) of diyah—i.e., the additional requirements for heavy diyah—was a matter of disagreement among the Companions of the Prophet. Among the various opinions, the Hanafi school has chosen to follow the view of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. This reflects the Hanafi methodology of giving weight to the opinions of the leading Companions, especially those known for their deep knowledge of fiqh. The specific details of Ibn Mas'ud's view are not mentioned here, but it likely pertains to the classification of camels or other conditions.

Key Terms
تغليظ (taghliz): Aggravation of diyah, i.e., making it heavier due to circumstances like intentional killing or sacred months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school follows the view of Ibn Mas'ud on the aggravation of diyah, a position that was not unanimous among the Companions.

The First Category of Camels in Diyah for Unintentional Killing: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on diyah for unintentional killing (khat') with a difference from Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the first camel category in khat' diyah and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For unintentional killing, Hanafis require younger male camels (ibn makhad) while Shafi'is require older ones (ibn labun).

The diyah (blood money) for unintentional killing (khat') is lighter than that for intentional killing. One key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools lies in the first category of camels that make up the diyah. This short passage highlights that difference, showing how a seemingly small variation in animal age can reflect broader methodological principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling context
Recognize that the passage discusses the diyah for khat' (unintentional killing), which is a lighter form of blood money. Note that the full diyah consists of 100 camels divided into categories.
The Hanafi school reduces the age requirement for the first category compared to the heavy diyah.
2
State the Hanafi position clearly
According to the Hanafi school, the first 20 camels of the khat' diyah are ibn makhad – a male camel that has completed one year. The remaining 80 camels come from the other four categories (20 each).
Ibn makhad is younger than the bint makhad (female one-year-old) used in the heavy diyah.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the first 20 camels should be ibn labun – a male camel that has completed two years. This is an older animal than the Hanafi requirement.
Ibn labun is the male equivalent of bint labun (female two-year-old).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference is that in Hanafi law, the blood money for unintentional killing requires younger (and thus less valuable) camels for the first category, while Shafi'is require older (more valuable) camels. This affects the total compensation amount to be paid.
The difference stems from varying interpretations of the hadith on diyah categories.
5
Understand the underlying reason for the difference
The Hanafi school considers that the lighter nature of khat' (unintentional) killing calls for a lighter diyah, hence using younger camels. The Shafi'i school, while also recognizing a lighter diyah, keeps the same category age as in the heavy diyah but switches to male camels.
This reflects different usul principles regarding the application of sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودِيَةُ الخطأ عندنا عشرون ابن مخاض : وهو ذكر تمت عليه حول، ومن الأصنافِ الأربعة المذكورة عشرون عشرون ، وعند الشافعي : عشرون ابن لبون مكان ابن مخاض.
And the diyah for error (khat') according to us is twenty ibn makhad: which is a male that has completed one year, and from the four mentioned categories twenty each. And according to al-Shafi'i: twenty ibn labun instead of ibn makhad.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for diyah in cases of unintentional killing (khat'), which is a lighter diyah compared to the heavy diyah for intentional killing. According to the Hanafi school, the diyah for khat' consists of 100 camels, but from each of the four categories mentioned earlier (bint makhad, bint labun, hiqqah, jadha'ah), only 20 are required (making 80 total?), but the text says 'twenty each from the four categories' which would be 80. However, the full diyah for khat' is 100 camels, so perhaps the remaining 20 are from a different category? The text is ambiguous. It states specifically that the first category is 20 ibn makhad (male one-year-old) instead of bint makhad. Then it says 'from the four mentioned categories twenty each', meaning 20 from each: ibn makhad (male one-year), ibn labun (male two-year?), hiqqah? and jadha'ah? Actually, the text says 'from the four mentioned categories twenty each', implying a total of 80. But the classic Hanafi view is that khat' diyah is 100 camels divided into 5 categories of 20: 20 ibn makhad, 20 ibn labun, 20 hiqqah, 20 jadha'ah, and 20 thaniyyah (or similar). The text here mentions only four categories, indicating a possible omission. However, it clearly states the difference with Shafi'i: Hanafis use ibn makhad (male one-year-old) for the first 20, while Shafi'is use ibn labun (male two-year-old). This change reflects the lighter nature of unintentional killing diyah.

Key Terms
ابن مخاض (ibn makhad): A male camel that has completed one year.
ابن لبون (ibn labun): A male camel that has completed two years.
دية الخطأ (diyat al-khat'): Blood money for unintentional killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 20 ibn labun (male two-year-old)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires male one-year-old camels (ibn makhad) as the first category in khat' diyah, while the Shafi'i school requires male two-year-old camels (ibn labun), reflecting a lighter valuation by Hanafis.

Diyah of Woman and Dhimmi: Half and Equal – The Hanafi Position
Ruling on diyah amounts for women and dhimmis with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the diyah of a woman and a dhimmi, and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki counter-arguments using textual and rational proofs.

Core Idea
A woman's diyah is always half; a dhimmi's diyah equals a Muslim's – both rooted in Sunnah and analogy.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents two key Hanafi rulings on diyah (blood money) that distinguish the school from others: the continuous halving of a woman's diyah for all injuries, and the equality of a dhimmi's diyah with a Muslim's. The commentator provides robust proofs, including hadith reports and rational demonstrations, to refute the Shafi'i and Maliki positions. In this lesson, we will dissect the arguments and understand the legal methodology behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
State the Hanafi position on woman's diyah (half of man's for life and limbs) and dhimmi's diyah (equal to Muslim).
These are the mufta bihi positions from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Analyze the woman's diyah dispute
Identify the Shafi'i objection (no halving below one-third) and examine the Hanafi proofs: report from Ali, absurdity argument, and inconsistency in Shafi'i's own method.
The Hanafi response uses both naqli and aqli arguments.
3
Analyze the dhimmi's diyah dispute
Identify the opposing view (Malik: half) and the Hanafi proofs: hadith of Ibn Abbas, practice of Abu Bakr and Umar, qiyas on property, and Quranic implication.
The Hanafi position is supported by multiple lines of evidence.
4
Evaluate the strength of proofs
Note that Hanafi relies on ahad hadith and rational arguments; Shafi'i relies on a different interpretation of 'Sunnah' (ascribes it to Zayd).
The Hanafi commentator claims the Shafi'i proof is weak because it contradicts reported practice of senior Companions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: for a woman's injury below one-third, Hanafi gives half, Shafi'i gives full; for a dhimmi's death, Hanafi gives equal to Muslim, Maliki gives half.
This difference matters in actual blood money awards in contexts where diyah is applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمرأة نصفُ ما للرّجل في دِيَةِ النَّفس وما دونها، وللدمي ما للمسلم وللمرأة نصفُ ما للرِّجلِ في دِيَةِ النَّفس وما دونها)، هذا عندنا"، وعند الشافعي (1) : دونَ الثَّلث لا ينصف.

[١]قوله : هذا عندنا ؛ روي ذلك عن علي موقوفاً ومرفوعاً، وقال الشافعي الثلث وما دون الثلث لا يتنصف لما روي عن سعيد بن المسيب له أنه السنة ، وقال الشافعي : السنة إذا أطلقت يراد بها سُنَّة النبي .
:
[ولنا]: ما روينا، وما روي أن كبار الصحابة له أفتوا بخلافه، ولو كان سُنّة النبي لما خالفوه ، وقوله : سُنَّةٌ محمول على أنّه سنّة زيد الله ؛ لأنه لم يرد إلا عنه موقوفا. الثاني : أنه يؤدّي إلى المحال، وهو ما إذا كان ألمها أشدّ ومصابها أكبر أن يقل أرشها . بيانه : أنه لو قطع أصبع منها يجب عشر من الإبل، وإذا قطع إصبعان يجب عشرون ، وإذا قطع ثلاثة يجب ثلاثون ؛ لأنها تساوي الرجل فيه على زعمه ؛ لكونه ما دونَ الثلث.
ولو قطع أربعة يجب عشرون ؛ للتنصيف فيما هو أكثر من الثلث، فقطع الرابعة لا يوجب شيئاً بل يسقط ما وجب بقطع الثالثة، وحكمة الشارع تنافي ذلك، فلا تجوزُ نسبته إليه ؛ لأن من المحال أن تكون الجناية لا توجب شيئاً شرعاً، وأقبح منه أن تسقط ما وجب لغيرها، وهذا مما تحيله العقلاء بالبداهة. الثالث : إن الشافعي هل يعتبر الأطراف بالأنفس وتركه هاهنا، حيث نصف دِيَة
النفس، ولم ينصف دِيَة الأطرافِ إلا إذا زاد على الثلث (۳).

[۲] قوله : هذا عندنا ؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى في مستأمن قتله عمرو بن أمية بمئة من الإبل ، وقال : «دِيَةُ كلّ ذي عهد في عهده ألف دينار»(4).
والنصراني أربعةُ الآف درهم، ودية المجوسي ثمانمئة درهم ، وعند مالك دية اليهودي والنصراني نصفُ دِيَة المسلم، ودية المسلم عنده اثنا عشر ألف درهم.
وعن الزهري له : «إن أبا بكر وعمر ه كانا يجعلان دية الذمي مثل دية المسلم»، وقال علي ه: «إنّما بذلوا الجزية لتكون دماؤهم كدمائنا وأموالهم كأموالنا»، وفي ظاهر قوله : وَإِن كَانَ مِن قَوْمِ بَيْنَكُمْ وَبَيْنَهُم مِّشَقٌ فَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَّمَةٌ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ ) (۲) ؛ دلالة عليه ؛ لأنّ المراد منه ظاهر ما هو المراد من قوله في قتل المؤمن : وَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَمَةُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ (۳) ؛ لأنهم معصومون متقومون لإحراز أنفسهم بالدار. فوجب أن يكونوا ملحقين بالمسلمين إذ يجب تقبلهم ما يجب تقبلهم لو كانوا مسلمين، ألا ترى أن أموالهم لما كانت معصومةً متقوّمة يجب بإتلافها ما يجب بإتلاف مال المسلم، فإذا كان هذا في أموالهم فما ظنّك في أنفسهم. هكذا في تكملة البحر»(4).
And for women, half of what is for men in the diyah of life and what is below it, and for the dhimmi, what is for the Muslim. This is our position, and according to al-Shafi'i: below one-third is not halved. ... [Commentary as in Arabic]
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an inter-madhhab dispute. It states two distinct rulings: (1) the diyah of a woman is half that of a man for both life and injuries below life, and (2) the diyah of a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) is the same as that of a Muslim. The author then notes that these are the Hanafi positions, contrasting with al-Shafi'i who holds that below one-third of the diyah, a woman's share is not halved. The commentary provides three Hanafi proofs against al-Shafi'i: first, citing reports from Ali (both mawquf and marfu') that the diyah of a woman is half; second, showing that al-Shafi'i's view leads to absurdity (e.g., cutting four fingers yields less than three); third, pointing out inconsistency in al-Shafi'i's own method. For the dhimmi ruling, the Hanafi proof includes a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet gave a diyah of 100 camels for a protected person (musta'min), and arguments from the practice of the early caliphs and from Quran 4:92.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money or monetary compensation paid to the heirs of a victim of homicide or injury.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen living under the protection (dhimma) of an Islamic state.
تنصيف (tansif): The legal principle of halving the diyah for women compared to men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the diyah of a dhimmi compared to a Muslim?
A) Half of the diyah of a Muslim
B) Equal to the diyah of a Muslim
C) Double the diyah of a Muslim
D) One-third of the diyah of a Muslim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's rulings on diyah—halving for women and equality for dhimmis—are supported by strong textual and rational proofs against opposing views.

Full Diyah for the Nose, Penis, and Glans: Hanafi Rules and the Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on full diyah for specific organs with Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which organs incur full diyah under Hanafi law and explain the Hanafi condition of functionality for the penis, as opposed to the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Full diyah for the penis depends on its capacity for insertion; a non-functional penis only merits just compensation.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the author's general ruling that full diyah is due for cutting the nose, penis, and glans. However, he qualifies that for the nose, there is a dispute over the bridge; for the penis, full diyah is conditional on sexual function. A key Hanafi-Shafi'i difference emerges: the Shafi'i school awards full diyah regardless of functionality, whereas the Hanafi school limits full diyah to functional loss. Understanding this distinction is critical for accurately applying the law of diyat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the organs and the general ruling
The passage lists four items: life (i.e., homicide), nose, penis, and glans. For each, the general rule is that full diyah (100 camels or equivalent) is due. However, the commentary immediately qualifies the nose and penis.
Note that 'life' refers to the diyah for wrongful death, which is full diyah for a free Muslim.
2
Examine the nose: differentiate parts
For the nose, full diyah is due for cutting the entire organ or the fleshy tip (marinn). For the bridge (arnaba), there is a dispute: some say full diyah, others say hukumat 'adl (just compensation). The commentator states the correct view is hukumat.
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf shows that not every part of the nose carries the same fixed compensation.
3
Examine the penis: the author's absolute statement
The author (al-Marghinani) stated that full diyah is due for the penis without differentiating conditions. The commentator criticizes this as too absolute and suggests a qualification: full diyah is due only if cutting the penis prevents insertion (i.e., eliminates sexual function).
The commentator's preferred phrase would be: 'By cutting the penis, insertion is prevented.'
4
Analyze the castrated/impotent case: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
For a castrated or impotent man, the Hanafi school (as per al-Muhit and the commentator) holds that only hukumat 'adl is due because the penis cannot achieve insertion. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for full diyah. The Hanafi response: full diyah is for the loss of a functional organ; without function, it is like a non-functional limb.
This is the central madhhab dispute in the passage.
5
Apply the functionality condition to sick and old men
For a sick person, full diyah is due because recovery is expected and the penis will regain function. For an old man, if the penis is immobile and incapable of intercourse, hukumat is due; if it can move and function, full diyah is due. The passage cuts off before completing the old man's case.
The principle is consistent: compensation follows functionality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النفس، والأنف، والذكر، والحشفة (٢) [١]قوله : والأنف ؛ أي في قطع الأنف دية كاملة، وكذلك في قطع مارنه وأرنبته، وقيل : في أرنبته حكومة عدل على الصحيح. And in [cases of] life, nose, penis, and glans (2) [1] His saying: 'and the nose': meaning that in cutting the nose, a full diyah is due, and similarly in cutting its fleshy tip and its bridge, and it is said: in its bridge, just compensation [hukumat 'adl] is correct. [2] His saying: 'and the penis and glans': the author made absolute regarding the obligation of diyah in the penis, and did not differentiate between young and old, nor between sick and healthy, nor between a castrated and impotent male, and it is necessary to clarify that, and if he had said: 'and by cutting the penis, insertion is prevented' it would be better. In al-Muhit: for the penis of a castrated and impotent male, just compensation, and from al-Shafi'i: full diyah. For us: the penis of a castrated and impotent male cannot conceive insertion by itself, so diyah is not obligatory; in the penis of a sick person, full diyah because after illness he returns to full strength; in the penis of an old man, if it cannot move and he has no ability for intercourse, just compensation, and if it moves and he is able to...
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on specific organs for which full diyah (blood money) is due: the entire life (i.e., homicide), the nose, the penis, and the glans (head of the penis). The commentary first explains that for the nose, full diyah is due for cutting the entire organ or its fleshy part (marinn) and bridge (arnaba), though some say just compensation for the bridge. For the penis and glans, the commentator notes that the author (al-Marghinani) did not differentiate based on age or health. The commentator prefers a qualification: full diyah is only due if cutting eliminates the ability to insert. He cites al-Muhit: for a castrated or impotent man, only just compensation (hukumat 'adl) is due, whereas al-Shafi'i argues for full diyah. The Hanafi response explains that a castrated or impotent penis cannot achieve insertion, so full diyah is not justified; for a sick person, full diyah is due because recovery is expected; for an old man, it depends on functionality—if immobile and incapable, just compensation; if capable, full diyah. The passage cuts off before completing the ruling for the old man.

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): Just compensation determined by a judge, based on the severity of injury and loss, as opposed to a fixed amount.
مارنة (marinnah): The fleshy tip of the nose.
أرنبة (arnabah): The bridge of the nose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Half diyah
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
Full diyah for the penis is conditional on its capacity for insertion; otherwise, only just compensation (hukumat) is due.

Diyah for Dhimmis and Majus: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling with proofs from hadith, Quran, and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi diyah amounts for a dhimmi and a Majusi, explain the proofs from hadith, Quran, and qiyas, and contrast with the Maliki position.

Core Idea
The diyah of a dhimmi is 4,000 dirhams; of a Majusi is 800 — based on equality in blood protection.

This passage presents the Hanafi position on blood money (diyah) for non-Muslim residents (dhimmis) and Zoroastrians (Majus). It not only states the amounts but provides solid textual proofs from the early caliphs, Ali ibn Abi Talib, and a Quranic verse, along with a qiyas from wealth. It also contrasts with Imam Malik’s view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi amounts
From the text, note that the diyah for a Christian dhimmi is 4,000 dirhams and for a Majusi is 800 dirhams.
2
Recognize the opposing view
Imam Malik holds the diyah for a dhimmi is half of a Muslim's diyah (6,000 dirhams).
3
Examine the hadith proof
Analyze the hadith from al-Zuhri about Abu Bakr and Umar equating dhimmi diyah to Muslim diyah, and Ali’s statement linking jizyah to equal protection.
4
Understand the Quranic indication
See how Quran 4:92 uses the same expression for diyah for a treaty-protected person as for a believer, implying equality.
5
Follow the qiyas argument
The text draws an analogy from wealth to life: if dhimmi wealth is protected like a Muslim's, then their lives are similarly valued.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنصراني أربعةُ الآف درهم، ودية المجوسي ثمانمئة درهم ، وعند مالك دية اليهودي والنصراني نصفُ دِيَة المسلم، ودية المسلم عنده اثنا عشر ألف درهم. (وفي النفس، والأنف، والذكر، والحشفة (٢) وعن الزهري له : «إن أبا بكر وعمر ه كانا يجعلان دية الذمي مثل دية المسلم»، وقال علي ه: «إنّما بذلوا الجزية لتكون دماؤهم كدمائنا وأموالهم كأموالنا»، وفي ظاهر قوله : وَإِن كَانَ مِن قَوْمِ بَيْنَكُمْ وَبَيْنَهُم مِّشَقٌ فَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَّمَةٌ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ ) (۲) ؛ دلالة عليه ؛ لأنّ المراد منه ظاهر ما هو المراد من قوله في قتل المؤمن : وَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَمَةُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ (۳) ؛ لأنهم معصومون متقومون لإحراز أنفسهم بالدار. فوجب أن يكونوا ملحقين بالمسلمين إذ يجب تقبلهم ما يجب تقبلهم لو كانوا مسلمين، ألا ترى أن أموالهم لما كانت معصومةً متقوّمة يجب بإتلافها ما يجب بإتلاف مال المسلم، فإذا كان هذا في أموالهم فما ظنّك في أنفسهم. هكذا في تكملة البحر».
And the Christian (dhimmi) is 4,000 dirhams, and the diyah of the Majusi is 800 dirhams, and according to Malik, the diyah of the Jew and Christian is half the diyah of a Muslim, and the diyah of a Muslim according to him is 12,000 dirhams. (And concerning the life, nose, penis, and glans) And from al-Zuhri: 'Abu Bakr and Umar used to make the diyah of the dhimmi like the diyah of a Muslim,' and Ali said: 'They only paid the jizyah so that their blood would be like our blood and their wealth like our wealth.' And in the apparent meaning of His saying: 'And if he belongs to a people between whom and you there is a treaty, then a diyah is to be handed over to his family' (Quran 4:92), there is an indication of that, because what is meant is apparently what is meant by His saying concerning the killing of a believer: 'and a diyah is to be handed over to his family' (Quran 4:92), because they are inviolable and of monetary value due to the protection of their persons by the abode of Islam. Therefore, they must be joined to the Muslims, since what is due from them is the same as what would be due from them if they were Muslims. Do you not see that since their wealth is inviolable and of monetary value, for its destruction is due what is due for destroying the wealth of a Muslim? So if this is the case with their wealth, what do you think about their lives? This is in Takmilat al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the diyah (blood money) for non-Muslim residents (dhimmis) and Magians (Majus). It first states the Hanafi position: the diyah for a Christian dhimmi is 4,000 dirhams, for a Majusi 800 dirhams. It contrasts this with Imam Malik's view that the diyah for a Jew or Christian is half that of a Muslim (6,000 dirhams). Then it provides proofs: a hadith from al-Zuhri that Abu Bakr and Umar set the diyah of a dhimmi equal to that of a Muslim, and a statement of Ali that jizyah is paid so that dhimmis' blood and wealth are protected like Muslims'. It then cites Quran 4:92, which mentions a diyah for a person from a people with whom there is a treaty, and argues that the same diyah wording is used for a believer, implying equality. The reasoning is that dhimmis are inviolable and their lives have monetary value due to the protection of the Islamic state, so they should be treated like Muslims. This is supported by a qiyas (analogy): if their wealth is protected and compensation for destroying it is like that for a Muslim's wealth, then their lives should be similar. The passage ends by referencing Takmilat al-Bahr.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation paid to the heirs of a victim of accidental homicide or injury.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living in an Islamic state under a covenant of protection (dhimma).
مجوسي (Majusi): A Zoroastrian; a follower of the Magian religion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 4,000 dirhams
C) 10,000 dirhams
D) Half of a Muslim's diyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes diyah for dhimmis at 4,000 dirhams and for Majus at 800 dirhams, based on scriptural and rational proofs that their blood is protected like Muslims'.

Diyah for Nose, Penis, and Glans
Rulings on diyah for nose, penis, and glans with intra-Hanafi details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi diyah for cutting nose, penis, and glans, and distinguish between full diyah and arbitration based on functionality.

Core Idea
Diyah depends on organ function: full diyah for nose and glans; for penis, only if functional.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on the matn's concise ruling on diyah for three specific body parts: the nose, the penis, and the glans. While the matn appears to prescribe full diyah categorically for the penis, the commentator introduces critical functional distinctions that reflect the Hanafi school's emphasis on the purpose of the organ. We will walk through these distinctions and their proofs, noting also the Shafi'i counterposition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the nose
The text states that cutting the nose incurs full diyah, including its fleshy part and tip, though there is a view that only arbitration applies to the tip alone. Establish the majority Hanafi position.
The 'correct view' favors full diyah for the entire nose.
2
Analyze the ruling for the penis
The matn gave absolute diyah; the commentator clarifies that functionality matters. Distinguish cases: castrated/impotent (arbitration), sick (full diyah after recovery), old man (arbitration if non-functional, full if functional).
The key is whether the penis can achieve intercourse by itself.
3
Examine the ruling for the glans
Cutting the glans alone gives full diyah. But if the glans was already cut and then the rest of the penis is cut, only arbitration applies.
The glans is the essential part for intercourse.
4
Compare with Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds full diyah for cutting the penis regardless of functionality. The Hanafi school disagrees based on the impossibility of intercourse in certain cases.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different interpretations of the purpose of the organ.
5
Understand the proof method
The Hanafi proof is talili (reasoning by cause): diyah is due for loss of function, not mere loss of tissue. For the penis, if function is absent, the full diyah is not warranted; instead, arbitration.
This is analogous to other organs where function determines compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النفس، والأنف، والذكر، والحشفة حسن الدراية لأواخر شرح الوقاية (1) 11) قوله : والأنف ; أي في قطع الأنف دية كاملة، وكذلك في قطع مارنه وأرنبته، وقيل : في أرنبته حكومة عدل على الصحيح. [٢]قوله : والذكر والحشفة ؛ أطلق المصنف له في وجوب الدية في الذكر، ولم يُفَرِّق بين شاب وشيخ، ولا بين مريض وصحيح، ولا بين ذكر خصي وعنين، ولا بُدَّ من بيان ذلك، ولو قال : وبقطع ذكر يفوت به الإيلاج لكان أولى، وفي «المحيط»: وفي ذكر الخصي والعنين حكومة عدل، وعن الشافعي : كمال الدية. لنا : ذكر الخصي والعنين لا يتصوَّرُ منه الإيلاج بنفسه، فلا تجب الدية، وفي ذكر المريض دِيَةٌ كاملة ؛ لأنه بزوال المرض يعود إلى قوته الكاملة، وفي ذكر الشيخ الكبير إن كان لا يتحرك ولا قدرة له على الوطء حكومة عدل، وإن كان يتحرك ويقدر على الوطء دية كاملة، وفي قطع الحشفة دية كاملة، وفي قطع الذكر المقطوع الحشفة حكومة عدل، وكذا في «التكملة».
And concerning the life, nose, penis, and glans. (11) His statement: 'and the nose' means that in cutting the nose there is full diyah, likewise in cutting its fleshy part (marin) and its tip (arrabah). And it is said: in its tip there is arbitration according to the correct view. [2] His statement: 'and the penis and glans'; the author made an absolute ruling regarding the obligation of diyah for the penis, and did not distinguish between a young man and an old man, nor between a sick and a healthy man, nor between a castrated man and an impotent man, and this must be clarified. If he had said: 'and by cutting a penis by which intercourse is lost' it would have been better. In al-Muhit: 'For the penis of a castrated man and an impotent man there is arbitration.' And from al-Shafi'i: full diyah. Our proof: the penis of a castrated man and an impotent man cannot be imagined to achieve intercourse by itself, so diyah is not obligatory. For the penis of a sick man, full diyah because when the illness leaves it returns to its full strength. For the penis of a very old man: if it cannot move and he has no ability for intercourse, then arbitration; if it can move and he has ability for intercourse, then full diyah. And in cutting the glans, full diyah. And in cutting a penis whose glans is already cut, arbitration. Likewise in al-Takmila.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on diyah for nose, penis, and glans. It opens by stating the matn: 'And concerning the life, nose, penis, and glans.' The commentator then explains that cutting the nose incurs full diyah, including its fleshy part (marin) and tip (arrabah), though there is a view that only arbitration applies to the tip. For the penis, the author of the matn made a general ruling of full diyah without distinguishing various conditions. The commentator criticizes this, saying it would be better to specify 'a penis by which intercourse is lost.' He then cites al-Muhit: for a castrated (khasay) or impotent ('unnin) man, there is arbitration, not full diyah. The Shafi'i school holds full diyah. The Hanafi argument: such a penis cannot achieve intercourse by itself, so diyah is not obligatory. For a sick man, full diyah applies because after recovery it regains full function. For an old man: if completely non-functional, arbitration; if functional, full diyah. Cutting the glans alone gives full diyah, but cutting a penis that already lacks its glans gives arbitration. The passage ends by referencing al-Takmila.

Key Terms
الأنف (al-anf): The nose; cutting it incurs full diyah.
الذكر (al-dhakar): The penis; diyah depends on its ability to enable intercourse.
الحشفة (al-hashafah): The glans of the penis; cutting it incurs full diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Half diyah
C) Arbitration (hukumat 'adl)
D) No diyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi diyah for the penis is not absolute; it depends on the organ's ability to enable intercourse, with arbitration applied when that function is absent.

Diyah for the Loss of the Five Senses and the Mind
Ruling on diyah for five senses and mind

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full diyah ruling for each of the five senses and the mind, and explain the reasoning given by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Loss of any sense or mind incurs full diyah — each is a complete benefit.

This passage expands on the ruling for the five senses and the mind. Each faculty is considered an independent, complete benefit; permanent loss of any one merits full diyah. The commentator provides specific reasoning for each: the mind as the basis of all actions, smell for perceiving odors, taste for flavors, and hearing/sight as complete faculties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items listed in the matn
The matn lists the mind, smell, taste, hearing, and sight — each eligible for diyah.
2
Understand the rationale for each
For the mind: its loss nullifies all limb benefits. For smell: loss of pleasant odor perception. For taste: loss of flavor perception. For hearing and sight: complete loss of the faculty.
The commentary provides a distinct reason for each sense.
3
Recognize the cumulative precedent from Umar
Umar gave four full diyahs for one blow that removed mind, speech, hearing, and sight — showing multiple losses incur multiple diyahs.
This reinforces that each faculty is an independent cause of diyah.
4
Derive the ruling
Full diyah is wajib for permanent loss of any one of these five senses or the mind.
The ruling applies even if the loss is from a single act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعقل، والشم والذوق، والسمع والبصر، واللسان إن منع النُّطق أو أداء أكثر الحروف، ولحية حلقت فلم تنبت ، وشعر الرأس الدية : أي الدية الكاملة . الوطء دية كاملة، وفي قطع الحشفة دية كاملة، وفي قطع الذكر المقطوع الحشفة حكومة عدل، وكذا في «التكملة»(۱). 11 ] قوله : والعقل والشم والذوق والسمع والبصر ; يعني تجب في كلّ واحدٍ منها دية كاملة، أما العقل فلان بذهابه تذهب منافع الأعضاء كلها ؛ لأن أفعال المجنون تجري مجرى أفعال البهائم. وأما الشم فلان بفواته يفوت إدراك الروائح الطيبة، والتفرقة بين الرائحة الطيبة والخبيثة. وأما الذوق ؛ فلأن لفواته يفوت إدراك الحلاوة والمرارة وغيرها. وأما السمع : فلأنه لفواته يفوتُ جنس المنفعة على الكمال، وهو الاستماع وهكذا البصر، وقد روي أن عمر الله قضى بأربع ديات في ضربة واحدة ذهب بها العقل والكلام والسمع والبصر. [٢] قوله : واللسان... الخ ؛ قال محمد الله في «الأصل»: وفي اللسان الدية، يريد به حالة الخطأ، وإذا قطعَ بعض اللسان إن منعه عن الكلام ففيه كمال الدية. وأما إذا منعه عن بعض دون البعض، فإنّه تجب الدية بقدر ما فات ، ففي النصف نصف الدية، وفي الربع الربع هكذا، وكيف تعرف مقدار الفائت من الباقي ؟ فيه اختلاف المتأخرين ، فصله صاحب تكملة البحر»(۳). [٣] قوله : ولحية حلقت فلم تنبت وشعر الرأس ; يعني إذا حلق اللحية فلم تنبت، أو حلق شعر الرأس ولم ينبت، ففي كلِّ واحدٍ منهما دية كاملة ؛ لأنه أزالَ الجمال على الكمال.
And the mind, smell, taste, hearing, sight, and the tongue if it prevents speech or the articulation of most letters, and a beard that is shaved and does not grow back, and hair of the head: the diyah, i.e., full diyah. The penis: full diyah; and in cutting the glans: full diyah; and in cutting a penis whose glans is cut: arbitration. Likewise in al-Takmila. (11) His statement: 'and the mind, smell, taste, hearing, and sight' means that for each one of them full diyah is obligatory. As for the mind, because with its loss all benefits of the limbs are lost, for the actions of an insane person are like the actions of animals. As for smell, because with its loss the perception of pleasant odors and the distinction between good and bad odors is lost. As for taste, because with its loss the perception of sweetness, bitterness, and others is lost. As for hearing, because with its loss the entire type of benefit is completely lost, which is listening, and likewise sight. It is narrated that Umar gave four full diyahs for one blow that took away the mind, speech, hearing, and sight. [2] His statement: 'and the tongue...' Muhammad al-Shaybani said in al-Asl: 'For the tongue, diyah,' meaning in the case of accidental injury. And if part of the tongue is cut and it prevents speech, then full diyah. But if it prevents some speech and not others, then diyah is due in proportion to what is lost: for half, half diyah; for a quarter, a quarter, and so on. How to determine the amount lost from the remaining? There is disagreement among later scholars, elaborated by the author of Takmilat al-Bahr. [3] His statement: 'and a beard that is shaved and does not grow back, and hair of the head' means that if one shaves the beard and it does not regrow, or shaves the hair of the head and it does not regrow, then for each one of them full diyah is due, because he has completely removed beauty.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings on diyah for sensory organs and hair. It first lists the mind, smell, taste, hearing, sight, and tongue (if it prevents speech), as well as a shaved beard or head hair that does not regrow — each incurs full diyah. The commentator explains each: for the mind, because insanity removes all benefits; for smell, because it distinguishes good and bad odors; for taste, for sweetness and bitterness; for hearing and sight, for the complete benefit of listening and seeing. He narrates that Umar gave four full diyahs for one blow that took away mind, speech, hearing, and sight. For the tongue, Imam Muhammad in al-Asl says diyah is due in accidental cases. If part of the tongue is cut and prevents full speech, full diyah applies; if partial, proportionate diyah. The method of determining the extent of loss is debated among later scholars. For the beard and head hair, if shaved and they do not regrow, full diyah is due because they completely remove beauty.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): The faculty of reason; its loss incurs full diyah.
الشم (al-sham): The sense of smell; its loss incurs full diyah.
الذوق (al-dhawq): The sense of taste; its loss incurs full diyah.
السمع (al-sam’): The sense of hearing; its loss incurs full diyah.
البصر (al-basar): The sense of sight; its loss incurs full diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why does loss of the mind incur full diyah?
A) Because it is one of the five senses
B) Because it is the basis of all human actions
C) Because it is the most important faculty
D) Because Umar ruled so

Key Takeaway
Full diyah is wajib for permanent loss of the mind or any of the five senses, each considered a complete benefit.

Diyah for the Tongue: Full and Proportional Compensation
Ruling on diyah for tongue with partial loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between complete and partial loss of tongue function and calculate proportional diyah.

Core Idea
Tongue diyah is full if speech is entirely lost; partial loss yields proportional compensation.

This passage focuses on diyah for the tongue. Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Asl specifies that diyah applies in accidental cases. The key point: if cutting part of the tongue prevents all speech, full diyah; if only partial, diyah is proportional to the loss. Determining the proportion is debated among later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling for the tongue
Full diyah is due if the tongue is cut and speech is completely lost.
Accidental injury assumption.
2
Understand partial loss
If only part of the tongue is cut and speech is partially affected, diyah is proportional to the loss (e.g., half tongue -> half diyah).
The text gives examples of half and quarter.
3
Recognize the measurement difficulty
Determining exactly how much speech is lost is debated among later scholars.
The author refers to Takmilat al-Bahr for elaboration.
4
Apply to cases
Estimate the proportion of speech lost and assign diyah accordingly.
Full diyah for complete loss; partial for incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعقل، والشم والذوق، والسمع والبصر، واللسان إن منع النُّطق أو أداء أكثر الحروف، ولحية حلقت فلم تنبت ، وشعر الرأس الدية : أي الدية الكاملة . الوطء دية كاملة، وفي قطع الحشفة دية كاملة، وفي قطع الذكر المقطوع الحشفة حكومة عدل، وكذا في «التكملة»(۱). 11 ] قوله : والعقل والشم والذوق والسمع والبصر ; يعني تجب في كلّ واحدٍ منها دية كاملة، أما العقل فلان بذهابه تذهب منافع الأعضاء كلها ؛ لأن أفعال المجنون تجري مجرى أفعال البهائم. وأما الشم فلان بفواته يفوت إدراك الروائح الطيبة، والتفرقة بين الرائحة الطيبة والخبيثة. وأما الذوق ؛ فلأن لفواته يفوت إدراك الحلاوة والمرارة وغيرها. وأما السمع : فلأنه لفواته يفوتُ جنس المنفعة على الكمال، وهو الاستماع وهكذا البصر، وقد روي أن عمر الله قضى بأربع ديات في ضربة واحدة ذهب بها العقل والكلام والسمع والبصر. [٢] قوله : واللسان... الخ ؛ قال محمد الله في «الأصل»: وفي اللسان الدية، يريد به حالة الخطأ، وإذا قطعَ بعض اللسان إن منعه عن الكلام ففيه كمال الدية. وأما إذا منعه عن بعض دون البعض، فإنّه تجب الدية بقدر ما فات ، ففي النصف نصف الدية، وفي الربع الربع هكذا، وكيف تعرف مقدار الفائت من الباقي ؟ فيه اختلاف المتأخرين ، فصله صاحب تكملة البحر»(۳). [٣] قوله : ولحية حلقت فلم تنبت وشعر الرأس ; يعني إذا حلق اللحية فلم تنبت، أو حلق شعر الرأس ولم ينبت، ففي كلِّ واحدٍ منهما دية كاملة ؛ لأنه أزالَ الجمال على الكمال.
And the mind, smell, taste, hearing, sight, and the tongue if it prevents speech or the articulation of most letters, and a beard that is shaved and does not grow back, and hair of the head: the diyah, i.e., full diyah. The penis: full diyah; and in cutting the glans: full diyah; and in cutting a penis whose glans is cut: arbitration. Likewise in al-Takmila. (11) His statement: 'and the mind, smell, taste, hearing, and sight' means that for each one of them full diyah is obligatory. As for the mind, because with its loss all benefits of the limbs are lost, for the actions of an insane person are like the actions of animals. As for smell, because with its loss the perception of pleasant odors and the distinction between good and bad odors is lost. As for taste, because with its loss the perception of sweetness, bitterness, and others is lost. As for hearing, because with its loss the entire type of benefit is completely lost, which is listening, and likewise sight. It is narrated that Umar gave four full diyahs for one blow that took away the mind, speech, hearing, and sight. [2] His statement: 'and the tongue...' Muhammad al-Shaybani said in al-Asl: 'For the tongue, diyah,' meaning in the case of accidental injury. And if part of the tongue is cut and it prevents speech, then full diyah. But if it prevents some speech and not others, then diyah is due in proportion to what is lost: for half, half diyah; for a quarter, a quarter, and so on. How to determine the amount lost from the remaining? There is disagreement among later scholars, elaborated by the author of Takmilat al-Bahr. [3] His statement: 'and a beard that is shaved and does not grow back, and hair of the head' means that if one shaves the beard and it does not regrow, or shaves the hair of the head and it does not regrow, then for each one of them full diyah is due, because he has completely removed beauty.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings on diyah for sensory organs and hair. It first lists the mind, smell, taste, hearing, sight, and tongue (if it prevents speech), as well as a shaved beard or head hair that does not regrow — each incurs full diyah. The commentator explains each: for the mind, because insanity removes all benefits; for smell, because it distinguishes good and bad odors; for taste, for sweetness and bitterness; for hearing and sight, for the complete benefit of listening and seeing. He narrates that Umar gave four full diyahs for one blow that took away mind, speech, hearing, and sight. For the tongue, Imam Muhammad in al-Asl says diyah is due in accidental cases. If part of the tongue is cut and prevents full speech, full diyah applies; if partial, proportionate diyah. The method of determining the extent of loss is debated among later scholars. For the beard and head hair, if shaved and they do not regrow, full diyah is due because they completely remove beauty.

Key Terms
اللسان (al-lisan): The tongue; diyah is due if it prevents speech or articulation of most letters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what diyah applies if half the tongue is cut and half of speech is lost?
A) Full diyah
B) Half diyah
C) Quarter diyah
D) Arbitration

Key Takeaway
Tongue diyah is full if speech is entirely lost; proportional (by functional loss) if partial.

Diyah for Beard and Head Hair: Permanent Loss of Beauty
Ruling on diyah for permanent hair loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling that full diyah is due for shaving a beard or head hair that does not regrow, and identify the condition of permanent non-regrowth.

Core Idea
Shaving a beard or head hair that never regrows incurs full diyah for removing beauty permanently.

This passage addresses the diyah for shaving a beard or head hair that does not grow back. The key condition: the hair does not regrow. If it regrows, no diyah. The justification is that beauty is completely and permanently removed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and target
The act is shaving the beard or head hair. The diyah is due only if the hair does not regrow.
The hair must be removed by another person (not self-harm).
2
Understand the condition for diyah
Diyah is wajib only if the hair does not grow back. If it regrows, there is no compensation.
Permanent loss is the trigger.
3
Recognize the rationale
The beard and head hair are sources of beauty; permanent removal removes that beauty entirely.
The text says 'because he has completely removed beauty.'
4
Apply the ruling
Full diyah for each: shaved beard that never regrows, shaved head hair that never regrows.
They are separate; two diyahs if both occur in one act.

Full Diyah for Senses, Tongue, Beard, and Head Hair
Expansion of diyah rulings with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on full diyah for loss of senses, tongue, beard, and head hair, and explain the proof from the saying of 'Ali (RA) and the school's rebuttal to the Maliki/Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Full diyah is wajib for loss of senses, tongue, and permanently lost beard/hair because they eliminate complete benefit or beauty.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah expands the matn's rulings on diyah for specific faculties and body parts. The author systematically lists the items for which a full diyah is obligatory, provides rationales, and addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding beard and head hair. Understanding these rulings helps you grasp how Hanafi fiqh values human wholeness and beauty in tort law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items for full diyah
Locate in the text the five senses (mind, smell, taste, hearing, sight) and the tongue, beard, and head hair. Note that each incurs a full diyah (100 camels) if permanently lost.
The text also mentions paired limbs and eyelashes; we'll cover those later.
2
Understand the rationale for each sense
For each sense, the commentator gives a reason: mind loss makes one like a beast, smell loss removes pleasant scent perception, taste loss removes flavor perception, hearing and sight loss remove complete benefit. This shows systematic valuation.
The report from 'Umar (RA) of four diyas for one blow reinforces this.
3
Analyze the tongue ruling
Full diyah is due if the tongue prevents speech entirely. If partial, diyah is proportional (e.g., half for half). The method of measuring lost function is disputed among later scholars.
This applies only in accidental (error) cases according to Muhammad al-Shaybani.
4
Examine the beard and head hair dispute
Hanafi: full diyah because complete beauty is removed. Maliki/Shafi'i: only hukumat al-adl (fair assessment). The Hanafi proof is the saying of 'Ali (RA) on a shaved head that doesn't regrow.
The text treats the mawquf narration as marfu' because it involves fixed measures (maqadir).
5
Apply the rule to paired organs and eyelashes
Destroying both of a pair (e.g., hands, eyes) requires full diyah; destroying one requires half. Cutting all eyelashes requires one full diyah as they are considered one entity.
This follows from the principle that each pair is a single benefit unit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات/ أنواعها وأحكامها
والعقل، والشم والذوق، والسمع والبصر، واللسان إن منع النُّطق أو أداء أكثر الحروف، ولحية حلقت فلم تنبت، وشعر الرأس الدية) : أي الدية الكاملة ، الوطء دية كاملة، وفي قطع الحشفة دية كاملة، وفي قطع الذكر المقطوع الحشفة حكومة عدل، وكذا في «التكملة». قوله : والعقل والشم والذوق والسمع والبصر؛ يعني تجب في كلّ واحدٍ منها دية كاملة، أما العقل فلان بذهابه تذهب منافع الأعضاء كلها؛ لأن أفعال المجنون تجري مجرى أفعال البهائم. وأما الشم فلان بفواته يفوت إدراك الروائح الطيبة، والتفرقة بين الرائحة الطيبة والخبيثة. وأما الذوق؛ فلأن لفواته يفوت إدراك الحلاوة والمرارة وغيرها. وأما السمع؛ فلأنه لفواته يفوتُ جنس المنفعة على الكمال، وهو الاستماع، وهكذا البصر، وقد روي أن عمر رضي الله قضى بأربع ديات في ضربة واحدة ذهب بها العقل والكلام والسمع والبصر. قوله : واللسان... الخ؛ قال محمد رحمه الله في «الأصل»: وفي اللسان الدية، يريد به حالة الخطأ، وإذا قطعَ بعض اللسان إن منعه عن الكلام ففيه كمال الدية. وأما إذا منعه عن بعض دون البعض، فإنّه تجب الدية بقدر ما فات، ففي النصف نصف الدية، وفي الربع الربع هكذا، وكيف تعرف مقدار الفائت من الباقي؟ فيه اختلاف المتأخرين، فصله صاحب تكملة البحر. قوله : ولحية حلقت فلم تنبت وشعر الرأس؛ يعني إذا حلق اللحية فلم تنبت، أو حلق شعر الرأس ولم ينبت، ففي كلِّ واحدٍ منهما دية كاملة؛ لأنه أزالَ الجمال على الكمال. كما في اثنين مما في البدن اثنان، وفي أحدهما نصفُها، وكما في أشفار العينين وعند مالك والشافعي: يجب في اللحية وشعرِ الرَّأسِ حكومة العدل. وقال مالك والشافعي رحمهما الله: فيهما حكومة عدل؛ لأنّ ذلك زيادة في الآدمي كشعر الصدر وغيره، ولنا: قول علي رضي الله له في الرأس إذا حلق ولم ينبت الدية كاملة، والموقوفُ فيها كالمرفوع؛ لأنه من المقادير، فلا يهتدى إليه بالرأي. وهذا كله إذا انْسَدَّ المنبت، فإن نَبَتَ حتى استوى كما كان لا يجب شيء؛ لأنه لم يبق بفعل الخالق أثر في البدن، ولكنّه يؤدِّبُ على ذلك. كذا في «التكملة»، ومثل الحلق النتف صرَّحَ به القُهُسْتَانِي. قوله : كما في اثنين ... الخ؛ أي يجب الدية الكاملة في إتلاف جميع العضوين الذين خُلقا في كل شخص اثنين كاليدين، والعينين، والشفتين، والحاجبين، والرجلين والأذنين والأنثيين، وثديي المرأة. كذا في «التبيين»، وفي إتلاف كل واحد من هذه الأشياء المزدوجة نصف الدية. قوله : وكما في أشفار العينين... الخ؛ الأشفار: جمع شفر: بالضم والفاء ساكنة: وهو طرف الجفن الذي ينبتُ عليه الشعر، وهو الهدب. كذا في «الصحاح»، وقد أخطأ بعضهم محمّداً رحمه الله في إطلاق الأشفار على الأهداب. وأجاب عنه صاحب «الهداية» بأنه يجوز أن يكون مراده الأهداب مجازاً للمجاورة، والحكم فيه هكذا، إذ لو قطعها جميعاً فيه دية واحدة؛ لأن الكل كشيء واحد.
The book of Diyat: Its Types and Rulings. And [for] the mind, smell, taste, hearing, sight, the tongue if it prevents speech or the performance of most letters, a beard that is shaved and does not grow back, and the hair of the head – the diyah (full blood money). That is, the complete diyah. Intercourse [requires] a complete diyah, and in cutting the glans [there is] a complete diyah, and in cutting a completely severed male organ [there is] a fair assessment (hukumat al-adl), and likewise in 'al-Takmilah'. He said: 'And the mind, smell, taste, hearing, sight' – meaning that for each one of them a complete diyah is obligatory. As for the mind, because with its loss the benefits of all limbs are lost; for the actions of an insane person resemble the actions of beasts. As for smell, because with its loss the perception of pleasant odors and the distinction between good and bad odors is lost. As for taste, because with its loss the perception of sweetness, bitterness, etc. is lost. As for hearing, because with its loss the complete kind of benefit is lost, which is listening, and similarly sight. And it has been reported that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) ruled for four diyahs in one blow that took away mind, speech, hearing, and sight. He said: 'And the tongue... etc.' Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said in 'al-Asl': And for the tongue [is] the diyah, meaning in the case of error. And if part of the tongue is cut, if it prevents speech, then there is a complete diyah. But if it prevents some [speech] but not all, then the diyah is obligatory in proportion to what is lost: for half, half the diyah; for a quarter, a quarter, and so on. And how is the amount of what is lost known from what remains? There is disagreement among the later scholars, and the author of 'Takmilat al-Bahr' detailed it. He said: 'And for a beard that is shaved and does not grow back, and the hair of the head' – meaning if one shaves the beard and it does not grow back, or shaves the hair of the head and it does not grow back, then for each one of them a complete diyah, because he has removed beauty completely. As in two limbs – what is in the body as two, and in one of them is half of it, and as in the eyelashes of the two eyes. And according to Malik and al-Shafi'i: For the beard and hair of the head, a fair assessment (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory. And Malik and al-Shafi'i said: There is a fair assessment for them, because that is an increase in the human like chest hair and others. And our evidence is the saying of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) concerning the head: if it is shaved and does not grow back, the complete diyah. And a mawquf [tradition] in this matter is like a marfu', because it is a matter of fixed measures (maqadir), not reached by opinion. This all applies if the hair follicle is blocked. If it grows back until it becomes as it was, nothing is obligatory, because no effect of the Creator's action remains on the body, but [the perpetrator] is disciplined for it. Thus in 'al-Takmilah'. And plucking is like shaving, as al-Quhustani explicitly stated. He said: 'As in two limbs... etc.' – meaning that a complete diyah is obligatory for destroying both of the limbs that are created as two in each person, like the hands, eyes, lips, eyebrows, feet, ears, testicles, and the breasts of a woman. Thus in 'al-Tabyin'. And for destroying each one of these paired things, half the diyah. He said: 'And as in the eyelashes of the two eyes... etc.' – al-ashfar is the plural of shufr: with a dammah on the shin and sukun on the fa', which is the edge of the eyelid upon which hair grows, and it is the eyelash. Thus in 'al-Sihah'. And some have mistakenly attributed to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) using 'ashfar' for 'ahdab'. The author of 'al-Hidayah' responded that it is permissible that he meant 'ahdab' metaphorically by contiguity, and the ruling is as follows: if they are all cut, there is a single diyah, because the whole is like one thing.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn's ruling on diyah (blood money) for specific faculties and body parts. The commentator begins by affirming that full diyah is wajib for the loss of mind, smell, taste, hearing, sight, the tongue (if it prevents speech or most letters), a shaved beard that does not regrow, and shaved head hair that does not regrow. For each of the five senses, the commentator provides a rationale: the mind's loss renders all limb benefits void, smell's loss removes perception of pleasant and unpleasant odors, taste's loss eliminates perception of flavors, hearing's loss removes the complete benefit of listening, and sight is similar. He also cites that 'Umar (RA) awarded four full diyahs for a single blow that caused loss of mind, speech, hearing, and sight. Regarding the tongue, the commentator clarifies that the ruling applies to accidental injury. If part of the tongue is cut and it prevents speech entirely, full diyah is due; if it prevents partial speech, the diyah is proportional (e.g., half for half, quarter for quarter). The method of determining the proportion is disputed among later scholars. For the beard and head hair, full diyah is wajib because shaving them removes complete beauty. The commentator then addresses a dispute with Maliki and Shafi'i schools, who hold that only a fair assessment (hukumat al-adl) is due, considering hair like chest hair (a mere adornment). The Hanafi proof is a saying of 'Ali (RA) that full diyah is due for a shaved head that does not regrow. This narration, though mawquf, is treated as marfu' because it concerns fixed legal measures (maqadir) that cannot be known by mere opinion. Finally, if the hair regrows normally, no diyah is due (as no permanent trace remains), but the perpetrator receives ta'zir (disciplinary punishment). Plucking is analogous to shaving. The commentator also notes that for paired body parts (e.g., hands, eyes, lips), destroying both requires full diyah, and destroying one requires half. For the eyelashes (ashfar), cutting all of them results in one full diyah, as they are considered a single entity.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money or financial compensation paid to the victim or heirs for bodily harm or homicide, typically 100 camels or equivalent.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): A fair assessment determined by a judge based on the nature of the injury, used when no fixed diyah is specified.
موقوف (mawquf): A narration attributed to a Companion but not explicitly to the Prophet (SAW).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone shaves another's beard and it does not regrow?
A) Nothing is due because it is a minor injury.
B) A fair assessment (hukumat al-adl) is due.
C) Full diyah (100 camels) is due.
D) Only ta'zir is required.

Key Takeaway
Full diyah (100 camels) is wajib for complete loss of senses, tongue, beard, and head hair in Hanafi fiqh, based on the principle that these are integral to human benefit and beauty.

Diyat for Hair: The Hanafi Position and the Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on diyat for hair with Hanafi position and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyat for head and beard hair, explain the proof from Ali (radi Allahu 'anhu), and apply the conditions (regrowth vs. permanent damage) to determine the outcome.

Core Idea
Full diyah for hair is wajib only if the follicle is permanently damaged and hair does not regrow.

The diyat (blood money) for injuries to the body generally follows fixed amounts for specific organs. However, when it comes to hair, there is a dispute: are fixed amounts applicable, or is an equitable assessment (hukumat al-adl) required? This lesson examines the Hanafi position, which relies on a statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib (radi Allahu 'anhu) treated as marfu', and contrasts it with the views of Malik and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: full diyah (10,000 dirhams) is wajib for removing head or beard hair if the hair does not regrow. If it regrows, no diyah but the perpetrator is disciplined.
This is the mufta bihi position from later Hanafi authorities like al-Quhistani and al-Takmilah.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that only hukumat al-adl (equitable assessment) is required, analogous to other body hair like chest hair.
Their reasoning is based on qiyas: since hair is not a vital organ, a fixed amount is not prescribed.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the statement of Ali (radi Allahu 'anhu): 'in the head if shaved and does not grow, full diyah.' Although this is mawquf (stopped at a Companion), it is treated as marfu' because matters of fixed quantities cannot be determined by personal opinion.
This type of inference is known as 'al-mawquf fi al-maqadir ka al-marfu'.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the opposing dalil
The Hanafi response distinguishes head and beard hair from other body hair due to their special significance (jamaal) and the existence of a specific textual proof from Ali. Quantities cannot be derived by analogy (qiyas) when a textual indication exists.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: fixed diyah vs. equitable assessment.
5
Apply the conditions
Determine whether the condition of permanent damage (insidad al-manbit) is met. If hair regrows fully, no diyah; if not, full diyah. Note that plucking is treated like shaving.
The discipline (ta'dib) is left to the judge's discretion when no financial compensation is due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال مالك والشافعي : فيهما حكومة عدل ؛ لأنّ ذلك زيادة في الآدمي كشعر الصدر وغيره، ولنا : قول علي الله له في الرأس إذا حلق ولم ينبت الدية كاملة، والموقوفُ فيها كالمرفوع ؛ لأنه من المقادير، فلا يهتدى إليه بالرأي. وهذا كله إذا انْسَدَّ المنبت ، فإن نَبَتَ حتى استوى كما كان لا يجب شيء؛ لأنه لم يبق بفعل الخالق أثر في البدن، ولكنّه يؤدِّبُ على ذلك. كذا في «التكملة»، ومثل الحلق النتف صرَّحَ به القُهُسْتَانِي.
Malik and al-Shafi'i said: In both (beard and head hair) there is an equitable assessment (hukumat al-adl), because that is an extra on the human like chest hair and others. And our proof: The statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding the head: if it is shaved and does not grow, the full diyah (is due). And a mawquf (tradition) in such matters is like a marfu' because it is about quantities, which cannot be determined by opinion. This all applies if the follicle is closed. If it grows back and becomes as it was, nothing is obligatory because no effect remains in the body from the perpetrator's action, but he is disciplined for it. Thus in al-Takmilah. And plucking is like shaving, as stated by al-Quhistani.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and the schools of Malik and al-Shafi'i regarding the diyat (blood money) for hair of the head and beard. The opponents argue that since hair is an additional feature like chest hair, its removal requires an equitable assessment (hukumat al-adl) rather than a fixed amount. The Hanafi response relies on a statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib (radi Allahu 'anhu) that if the head is shaved and hair does not regrow, full diyah is due. Although this statement is mawquf (stopped at a Companion), it is treated as marfu' (raised to the Prophet) because such matters of quantity cannot be based on opinion. The Hanafi ruling then clarifies conditions: if the hair follicle is permanently damaged and hair does not regrow, full diyah is wajib. If hair regrows completely, no diyah is due, but the perpetrator is disciplined (ta'dib). Plucking is analogous to shaving.

Key Terms
حكومة العدل (hukumat al-adl): An equitable assessment of the loss by a qualified expert, not a fixed amount.
المنبت (al-manbit): The place where hair grows, i.e., the hair follicle.
الموقوف (al-mawquf): A tradition that is narrated from a Companion, not explicitly from the Prophet.
المرفوع (al-marfu'): A tradition attributed directly to the Prophet.
التأديب (al-ta'dib): Disciplinary punishment, not fixed compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full diyah is wajib
B) Hukumat al-adl is wajib
C) Nothing is wajib but the perpetrator is disciplined
D) Half diyah is wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that full diyah for head and beard hair is due only when the follicle is permanently damaged and hair does not regrow; otherwise, only discipline is imposed.

Diyah for Paired Organs and Eyelids
Expansion of diyah rulings for paired organs and eyelids

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi diyah rulings for destroying paired organs and calculate the diyah for one or more eyelids.

Core Idea
Destroying both of a paired organ incurs full diyah; destroying one incurs half. For four eyelids, full diyah for all, quarter each.

This lesson explains the Hanafi rulings on diyah (blood money) for organs that come in pairs and for the eyelids. Understanding these fixed amounts is essential for accurate legal compensation in cases of bodily harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the paired organs
Read the list of paired organs mentioned in the passage: hands, eyes, lips, eyebrows, feet, ears, testicles, and female breasts.
These are all created in twos in every person.
2
Understand the diyah for a pair
For destroying both of any paired organ, full diyah is wajib. For destroying one of them, half diyah is wajib.
This applies uniformly to all listed paired organs.
3
Analyze the eyelid case
The four eyelids (upper and lower of each eye) are considered one unit. Destroying all four incurs full diyah. Destroying one eyelid incurs a quarter diyah, two incurs half, three incurs three-quarters.
The ruling is based on the number four, not on the pairing of eyes.
4
Note the linguistic clarification
The term ashfar is used metaphorically for eyelashes (ahlab). This was criticized but accepted due to adjacency.
The ruling remains valid regardless of the linguistic point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1] قوله : كما في اثنين ... الخ ؛ أي يجب الدية الكاملة في إتلاف جميع العضوين الذين خُلقا في كل شخص اثنين كاليدين، والعينين، والشفتين، والحاجبين، والرجلين والأذنين والأنثيين، وثديي المرأة. كذا في «التبيين»، وفي إتلاف كل واحد من هذه الأشياء المزدوجة نصف الدية. [٢] قوله : وكما في أشفار العينين... الخ ؛ الأشفار : جمع شفر: بالضم والفاء ساكنة : وهو طرف الجفن الذي ينبتُ عليه الشعر، وهو الهدب. كذا في «الصحاح»، وقد أخطأ بعضهم محمّداً لله في إطلاق الأشفار على الأهداب. وأجاب عنه صاحب «الهداية» بأنه يجوز أن يكون مراده الأهداب مجازاً للمجاورة، والحكم فيه هكذا، إذ لو قطعها جميعاً فيه دية واحدة ؛ لأن الكل كشيء واحد. كذا في «الأكملية»، وفي واحد منها ربع الدية ؛ لأنّ الأشفار أربعة، وفي اثنين نصف الدية، وفي الثلاثة ثلاثة أرباع كذا في «التبيين».
His saying: 'As in two...' means: full diyah is obligatory for destroying both organs that are created in pairs in every person, such as the two hands, two eyes, two lips, two eyebrows, two feet, two ears, two testicles, and two breasts of a woman. Thus in al-Tabyin. And for destroying each one of these paired things, half diyah. His saying: 'And as in the eyelids of the eyes...' al-ashfar is plural of shifr: with dammah and sukun on the fa', meaning the edge of the eyelid upon which hair grows, i.e., the eyelash. Thus in al-Sihah. And some have erred against Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) in using ashfar for ahlab (eyelashes). The author of al-Hidayah answered that it is permissible that he meant ahlab metaphorically by contiguity. The ruling is as follows: if one cuts all of them, there is one full diyah because all is like one thing. Thus in al-Akmaliyyah. And for one of them, a quarter of diyah because the eyelids are four; for two, half diyah; for three, three quarters. Thus in al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory comment on the base text, expounding the diyat for paired organs. It first lists organs that come in pairs: hands, eyes, lips, eyebrows, feet, ears, testicles, and female breasts. Destroying both requires full diyah; destroying one requires half. The comment then discusses eyelids (ashfar). It clarifies the linguistic meaning: ashfar are the edges of the eyelids where eyelashes grow. Some criticized Imam Muhammad for using 'ashfar' to mean eyelashes, but the answer from al-Hidayah is that it is a metaphorical usage due to adjacency. The ruling: the four eyelids (upper and lower of each eye) are considered as one unit such that destroying all four incurs one full diyah; destroying one eyelid incurs a quarter, two incur half, three incur three-quarters. This is based on the number four.

Key Terms
الأشفار (al-ashfar): Plural of shifr: the edges of the eyelids where lashes grow; here used metaphorically for the eyelashes themselves.
المزدوج (al-muzdawij): Paired organs, each created in twos in every person.

Key Takeaway
The diyah for paired organs is full for both, half for one; for the four eyelids, it is full for all four and quarter each.
