Section on the fetus. Whoever strikes a woman's abdomen and she miscarries a fetus, a ghurrah of five hundred dirhams is due on his aqilah if she miscarries it dead, and full diyah if she miscarries it alive and it dies. [2] Section on the fetus. And whoever strikes a woman's abdomen and she miscarries a fetus, a ghurrah of five hundred dirhams is due on his aqilah if she miscarries it dead, and full diyah if she miscarries it alive and it dies: meaning full diyah is due if she miscarries it alive and it dies because its death is due to the strike. And know that the ghurrah according to us is due over three years, for he made the ghurrah on the aqilah over three years. Also it is a substitute for a limb in some respects, and whatever is a substitute for a limb is due over three years if it is one-third of the diyah or less down to half a tenth. [1] His saying: ghurrah – with damm of the ghayn and fatha of the ra' mushaddadah – means five hundred dirhams here. And it is called ghurrah because it is the smallest of the amounts in diyat, and the smallest thing is its beginning in existence, and it is called ghurrah meaning the first; for this reason the first of the month is called ghurrah, and a person's face is called ghurrah because it is the first thing that appears from him. And qiyas would require that nothing be due because his life was not certain. If it is said: the apparent is that it was alive. We say: the apparent is not a valid proof for entitlement. And the basis of istihsan is what is narrated in the Sahihain from Abu Hurairah (RA) that the Prophet ﷺ judged for the fetus of a woman from Banu Lihyan a ghurrah of a slave or a slave-girl. And Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated in his Musannaf from Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash from Zayd ibn Aslam that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) valued the ghurrah at fifty dinars, each dinar being ten dirhams. And al-Bazzar narrated in his Musnad from 'Abdullah ibn Buraydah from his father that a woman threw a stone at a woman and the Prophet ﷺ judged for her child with five hundred and forbade throwing stones. And Abu Dawud narrated in his Sunan from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that he said: the ghurrah is five hundred dirhams. So we left qiyas for the athar, and it is a proof against Malik and al-Shafi'i (RA) who estimated it at six hundred. Thus in some commentaries of al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This lesson deals with the fetus (janin). If a person strikes a pregnant woman's abdomen, causing her to miscarry, two scenarios: (a) if the fetus is born dead, a ghurrah is due—500 dirhams—on the aqilah of the striker; (b) if the fetus is born alive and then dies, full diyah (10,000 dirhams or equivalent) is due. The ghurrah is paid in installments over three years (like other diyat up to one-third). The word ghurrah originally means the beginning or best part of something; here it refers to a payment of 500 dirhams, the minimum amount in diyah. The proof includes a hadith from the Sahihain: the Prophet ﷺ judged for the fetus of a woman from Banu Lihyan a ghurrah of a slave or a slave-girl, which was valued at 500 dirhams. Also, reports from Umar ibn al-Khattab and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i specify the amount as 500 dirhams. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas, because qiyas would suggest no payment is due since the fetus's life was not certain. The Hadith overrides qiyas. The Hanafi school holds that the ghurrah is 500 dirhams, while Malik and al-Shafi'i set it at 600 (or equivalent). The evidence for 500 is the explicit sum from the aforementioned reports.

Key Terms
جنين (janīn): fetus in the womb
غرة (ghurra): a payment of 500 dirhams for causing miscarriage of a dead fetus

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the amount of ghurrah for a miscarried dead fetus according to the Hanafi school?
A) 500 dirhams
B) 1000 dirhams
C) Full diyah
D) 600 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a stillborn fetus from a strike warrants a ghurrah of 500 dirhams based on istihsan from the Prophet's hadith, whereas a live-born death warrants full diyah.
